# 2.5 Rx power scaling EFS

## 2.5.1 Overview

### 2.5.1.0-1 Overview 5G-L1-UL performs a number of signal and noise power measurements, that are reported to 5G-L2-PS. It is the purpose of this section to explain how these measurements are scaled by L1-SW in order to be expressed in meaningful units (mW, dBm,…). A simplified view of the Rx processing chain (some operations not related to power adjustment are omitted) is shown in the next figures, for the CPRI and eCPRI cases, with an indication of the parameters that come into play as far as Rx power scaling is concerned. These parameters will be introduced in section 11418467 . They need to be known by L1-SW so that it can compute absolute Rx power levels in dBm or mW and report them to 5G-L2-PS. (ID: 11418368)

[image-0][image\_desc]The image is a flowchart illustrating a signal processing pipeline. At the top, there are several input parameters represented by rounded rectangles: "rx ScalingFactor", "fftScalingFactor", "2(3-agcshift Channel Type)", "alphaAgcChannelType", and "xScale".
To the left, a large light blue rounded rectangle contains the text "Radio Unit", suggesting it's a source or a component of the system.
The main processing pipeline is enclosed within a larger light blue rounded rectangle. Inside this area, there are five yellow rounded rectangles representing processing steps, connected by arrows indicating the flow of data. These steps are:
1. "FFT" (Fast Fourier Transform)
2. "RB Demapping"
3. "Post FFT AGC" (Automatic Gain Control)
4. "TOC" (likely "Time of Capture" or a similar time-domain operation)
5. "Per channel processing"
Arrows show that the "Radio Unit" feeds into the "FFT" block. The "fftScalingFactor" parameter also appears to influence the "FFT" block, as indicated by an arrow pointing from it to the "FFT" block. The "rx ScalingFactor" parameter also seems to be an input to the "FFT" block.
The output of "FFT" goes to "RB Demapping". The output of "RB Demapping" goes to "Post FFT AGC". The output of "Post FFT AGC" goes to "TOC". Finally, the output of "TOC" goes to "Per channel processing".
The parameters "2(3-agcshift Channel Type)", "alphaAgcChannelType", and "xScale" are shown with arrows pointing towards the "Post FFT AGC" and "TOC" blocks, suggesting they are configuration or control inputs for these stages. Specifically, "2(3-agcshift Channel Type)" and "alphaAgcChannelType" seem to influence "Post FFT AGC", while "xScale" appears to influence "TOC".[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2985.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]

Figure 1: Simplified view of Rx processing chain with indication of the main power scaling parameters (CPRI case, Traffic Channel)

[image-1][image\_desc]The image is a flowchart illustrating a signal processing pipeline. The pipeline starts with a "Radio Unit" on the left. Above the main processing block, there are several input parameters represented by rounded rectangles: "rxScalingFactor", "decimationFactor", "postFftScalingFactor", "postifftScalingFactor", and "max\_shift, ant\_shift".
The main processing block, enclosed in a light blue rounded rectangle, contains a sequence of operations represented by yellow rounded rectangles. These operations are connected by arrows indicating the flow of data. The sequence is as follows:
1. **Freq Shift (long format)**: This is the first operation in the sequence.
2. **Decimation (long format)**: This operation follows the frequency shift.
3. **FFT**: The Fast Fourier Transform is applied next.
4. **Post-FFT AGC**: Automatic Gain Control is applied after the FFT.
5. **IFFT power**: The Inverse Fast Fourier Transform and power calculation are performed.
6. **Non-coherent combining**: This operation combines signals non-coherently.
7. **Detector**: The final stage of the pipeline is the detector.
Arrows from the input parameters point to specific stages in the processing block, indicating that these parameters influence those operations. Specifically:
\* "rxScalingFactor" points to "Freq Shift".
\* "decimationFactor" points to "Decimation".
\* "postFftScalingFactor" points to "FFT".
\* "postifftScalingFactor" points to "IFFT power".
\* "max\_shift, ant\_shift" points to "Non-coherent combining".[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2985.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]

Figure 2: Simplified view of Rx processing chain with indication of the main power scaling parameters (CPRI case, PRACH TDD)

To the right of the "Radio Unit," there are several oval shapes containing text: "rxScalingFactor," "2-shift," "2(3-agcshiftChannelType)," "alphaAgcChannelType," and "xScale." These likely represent configuration parameters or control signals.
The main processing flow is contained within a larger light blue rounded rectangle. Inside this area, there are five yellow rounded rectangles, each representing a processing stage, connected by arrows indicating the data flow:
1. **IQ decompression**: This stage receives input from the "Radio Unit" and also has an incoming arrow from the "2-shift" oval.
2. **RB Demapping**: This stage receives input from "IQ decompression."
3. **Post FFT AGC**: This stage receives input from "RB Demapping" and also has an incoming arrow from the "2(3-agcshiftChannelType)" oval.
4. **TOC**: This stage receives input from "Post FFT AGC" and has an incoming arrow from the "alphaAgcChannelType" oval.
5. **Per channel processing**: This stage receives input from "TOC" and also has an incoming arrow from the "xScale" oval.
The arrows suggest a sequential processing order from left to right, with some stages also receiving external configuration or control inputs.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2985.004.png[/image\_path][/image-2]

[image-3][image\_desc]The image is a flowchart illustrating a signal processing pipeline. The pipeline starts with a "Radio Unit" on the left, which feeds into a series of processing blocks enclosed within a light blue rectangle. These blocks are arranged horizontally and are colored orange with rounded corners.
The processing blocks are:
1. "IQ decompression"
2. "Post-FFT AGC"
3. "IFFT power"
4. "Non-coherent combining"
5. "Detector"

1. "rx ScalingFactor"
2. "2-shit"
3. "postifftScalingFactor"
4. "max\_shift, ant\_shift"
Arrows indicate the flow of data. The "Radio Unit" output connects to "IQ decompression". The output of "IQ decompression" connects to "Post-FFT AGC", and so on, until the "Detector". The three input parameters ("rx ScalingFactor", "2-shit", "postifftScalingFactor", and "max\_shift, ant\_shift") have arrows pointing to specific processing blocks within the pipeline, suggesting they are control or configuration inputs for those blocks. Specifically, "rx ScalingFactor" points to "IQ decompression", "2-shit" points to "IQ decompression", "postifftScalingFactor" points to "IFFT power", and "max\_shift, ant\_shift" points to "Non-coherent combining".[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2985.005.png[/image\_path][/image-3]

[image-1][image\_desc]The image is a flowchart illustrating a signal processing pipeline. The pipeline starts with a "Radio Unit" which feeds into a "RACH ULFE" block. This block contains a "Sample Rate Convert" process. The output of "RACH ULFE" goes to a "TRICH ULFE" block, which includes "ISS" and "FFT" processes. The output of "TRICH ULFE" then enters a "PRCH" block, containing "ZC correlation & IFFT", "coherent Combining", "Noise Estimation", and "Peak detection" processes. Finally, the output of "PRCH" leads to an "MDAB" block, which performs "Power reports".
Several parameters are shown above the pipeline, connected by arrows to various stages:
- "rxScalingFactor" is connected to "RACH ULFE".
- "decimateScalingFactor" is connected to "RACH ULFE".
- "inputGainChannelType" is connected to "RACH ULFE".
- "fftScalingFactor" is connected to "TRICH ULFE".
- "prchScalingFactor" is connected to "PRCH".
- "zcSeqCorrScale" is connected to "PRCH".
- "cohCombScale" is connected to "PRCH".
- "otherScales" is connected to "PRCH".
There are also two arrows labeled "m" and "t" originating from the "PRCH" block and pointing towards the "MDAB" block.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2987.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]

Inside "RACH ULFE", there's a "Sample Rate Convert" process. The output of "RACH ULFE" goes to a block labeled "PRCH or MDAB/". This block contains two sequential processes: "Time AGC" followed by "FFT". The output of the "FFT" process then feeds into a block labeled "PRCH". Within the "PRCH" block, there are four sequential processes: "ZC correlation & IFFT", "coherent Combining", "Noise Estimation", and "Peak detection". Finally, the output of the "Peak detection" process is fed into a block labeled "MDAB", which contains a "Power reports" process.
Several external parameters are shown influencing different stages of the pipeline:
- "rxScalingFactor" influences "RACH ULFE".
- "decimateScalingFactor" influences "RACH ULFE".
- "prachTimeAgcGain" influences "RACH ULFE".
- "fftScalingFactor" influences "PRCH or MDAB/".
- "zcSeqCorrScale" influences "PRCH".
- "prchScalingFactor" influences "PRCH".
- "cohCombScale" influences "PRCH".
- "otherScales" influences "PRCH".

Here's a breakdown of the elements:
\* **rxScalingFactor**: A rounded rectangle at the top left, labeled "rxScalingFactor".
\* **Radio Unit**: A large light blue rounded rectangle on the left, labeled "Radio Unit". An arrow originates from "rxScalingFactor" and points towards "Radio Unit", suggesting it's an input or configuration parameter.
\* **MDAB (first instance)**: A large light blue rounded rectangle in the center, labeled "MDAB". Inside this box are two yellow rounded rectangles:
\* **RE demapping**: The first yellow rectangle, labeled "RE demapping". An arrow flows from "Radio Unit" into this box.
\* **Freq AGC**: The second yellow rectangle, labeled "Freq AGC". An arrow flows from "RE demapping" into this box. There is also an arrow originating from "nShift" pointing to "Freq AGC".
\* **nShift**: A rounded rectangle at the top center, labeled "nShift".
\* **MDAB (second instance)**: A large light blue rounded rectangle on the right, labeled "M DAB". Inside this box is a single yellow rounded rectangle:
\* **Power measurements and reports**: Labeled "Power measurements and reports". An arrow flows from "Freq AGC" into this box.
The overall flow suggests that the "Radio Unit" processes signals, which are then demapped and subjected to frequency AGC within the first "MDAB" block. The "rxScalingFactor" and "nShift" appear to be control or configuration inputs to the system. The processed signal then goes to the second "MDAB" block for power measurements and reporting.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2987.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3]

[image-0][image\_desc]The image is a flowchart illustrating a signal processing pipeline. The flowchart consists of several interconnected boxes and rounded rectangles, representing different processing stages and parameters. The background is a solid gray color.
From left to right, the flowchart begins with a rounded rectangle labeled "rxScalingFactor" with an arrow pointing down to a blue rounded rectangle labeled "Radio Unit".
To the right of "Radio Unit", there is a blue rounded rectangle labeled "ULFE" containing an orange rounded rectangle labeled "FFT". An arrow labeled "CPRI" connects "Radio Unit" to "ULFE".
To the right of "ULFE", there is a blue rounded rectangle labeled "SDEC" containing an orange rounded rectangle labeled "Symbol decompression". An arrow labeled "IQFP" connects "ULFE" to "SDEC".
Further to the right, there is a blue rounded rectangle labeled "MDAB" containing an orange rounded rectangle labeled "Freq AGC". An arrow labeled "eFXP" connects "SDEC" to "MDAB".
Finally, to the right of the first "MDAB" box, there is another blue rounded rectangle labeled "MDAB" containing an orange rounded rectangle labeled "Power measurements and reports". An arrow connects the "Freq AGC" box to this final "MDAB" box.
Above the flowchart, there are three more rounded rectangles: "fftScalingFactor" with an arrow pointing down to "ULFE", "comExp" with an arrow pointing down to "SDEC", and "nShift" with an arrow pointing down to the first "MDAB" box containing "Freq AGC".
The overall flow represents data processing from a radio unit through various stages of signal processing, including FFT, symbol decompression, frequency AGC, and finally power measurements and reports.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2989.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]

[image-1][image\_desc]The image is a flowchart illustrating a signal processing pipeline. The flowchart is organized with oval shapes representing scaling factors and rectangular shapes representing processing blocks. The processing blocks are further grouped into larger rectangular areas.
Here's a breakdown of the elements:
**Scaling Factors (Ovals):**
\* rxScalingFactor
\* decimateScalingFactor
\* fftScalingFactor
\* fdAgcGain
\* prchScalingFactor
\* cohCombScale
\* zcSeqCorrScale
\* nonCohCombScale
\* otherScales
**Processing Blocks and Groups:**
1. **Radio Unit:** A blue rectangular block on the left, labeled "Radio Unit". An arrow labeled "CPRI" points from it to the next stage.
2. **ULFE (First Instance):** A larger blue rectangular block containing a smaller orange rectangular block.
\* **ULFE:** Label for the larger blue block.
\* **Sample Rate Convert:** Label for the inner orange block. An arrow from "decimateScalingFactor" points to the "ULFE" block. An arrow from "rxScalingFactor" points to the "Radio Unit" block.
3. **ULFE (Second Instance):** Another larger blue rectangular block containing a smaller orange rectangular block.
\* **ULFE:** Label for the larger blue block.
\* **FFT:** Label for the inner orange block. An arrow labeled "IQFP" points from the first "ULFE" block to this second "ULFE" block. An arrow from "fftScalingFactor" points to this "ULFE" block.
4. **PRCH:** A large blue rectangular block containing several smaller orange rectangular blocks arranged horizontally. Arrows from various scaling factors point to this "PRCH" block and its internal components.
\* **PRCH:** Label for the larger blue block.
\* **coherent combining:** The first orange block within "PRCH". An arrow from "cohCombScale" points to it.
\* **FD AGC:** The second orange block within "PRCH". An arrow from "fdAgcGain" points to it.
\* **ZC correlation & IFFT:** The third orange block within "PRCH". An arrow from "zcSeqCorrScale" points to it.
\* **non-coherent combining:** The fourth orange block within "PRCH". An arrow from "nonCohCombScale" points to it.
\* **NPE & Peak Detection:** The fifth orange block within "PRCH". An arrow from "prchScalingFactor" points to the "PRCH" block, and an arrow from "otherScales" points to this "NPE & Peak Detection" block.
5. **MDAB:** A blue rectangular block on the right, containing a smaller orange rectangular block.
\* **MDAB:** Label for the larger blue block.
\* **Power measurements and reports:** Label for the inner orange block. An arrow points from the "NPE & Peak Detection" block to the "MDAB" block.
The overall flow starts from the "Radio Unit", goes through two "ULFE" stages, then into the "PRCH" block with its sequential processing steps, and finally to the "MDAB" block for measurements and reports. Various scaling factors influence different stages of the pipeline.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2989.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]

Figure 12: Simplified view of Rx processing chain with indication of the main power scaling parameters (CPRI case, PRACH channel)

[image-2][image\_desc]The image is a flowchart illustrating a signal processing pipeline. The flowchart is composed of several rectangular and oval shapes connected by arrows, representing different stages and data flows. The background is a solid gray color.
Here's a breakdown of the elements:
**Oval Shapes (Inputs/Parameters):**
\* **rxScalingFactor:** Located at the top left, with a downward arrow pointing to "Radio Unit".
\* **comExp:** Located at the top center, with a downward arrow pointing to "SDEC".
\* **nShift:** Located at the top right, with a downward arrow pointing to "MDAB".
**Rectangular Shapes (Processing Stages):**
\* **Radio Unit:** A blue rectangle on the left, receiving input from "rxScalingFactor". An arrow labeled "eCPRI" points from "Radio Unit" to "EDEC".
\* **EDEC:** A larger blue rectangle containing a smaller orange rectangle.
\* **eCPRI decompression:** The orange rectangle inside "EDEC", representing a specific processing step. An arrow labeled "IQFP" points from "EDEC" to "SDEC".
\* **SDEC:** A larger blue rectangle containing a smaller orange rectangle.
\* **Symbol decompression:** The orange rectangle inside "SDEC", representing a specific processing step. It receives input from "comExp". An arrow labeled "eFXP" points from "SDEC" to the first "MDAB".
\* **MDAB (first instance):** A larger blue rectangle containing a smaller orange rectangle.
\* **Freq AGC:** The orange rectangle inside this "MDAB", representing a specific processing step. It receives input from "nShift". An arrow points from this "MDAB" to the second "MDAB".
\* **MDAB (second instance):** A larger blue rectangle containing a smaller orange rectangle.
\* **Power measurements and reports:** The orange rectangle inside this "MDAB", representing the final processing step.
**Arrows (Data Flow):**
The arrows indicate the direction of data flow between the different components. The labels on some arrows specify the type of data being transferred (e.g., "eCPRI", "IQFP", "eFXP").
The overall flow starts with "Radio Unit" and progresses through "EDEC", "SDEC", and two instances of "MDAB", with external parameters influencing some of these stages.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2989.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2]

Figure 13: Simplified view of Rx processing chain with indication of the main power scaling parameters (eCPRI case, traffic channel)

[image-3][image\_desc]The image is a flowchart illustrating a signal processing pipeline. The flowchart is organized into several blocks, with arrows indicating the flow of data and control signals.
The main components of the flowchart are:
1. **Radio Unit**: A blue rounded rectangle on the left, labeled "Radio Unit". An arrow originates from "rxScalingFactor" and points to this block.
2. **EDEC**: A larger blue rounded rectangle containing a yellow rounded rectangle labeled "eCPRI decompression". An arrow labeled "eCPRI" connects "Radio Unit" to "EDEC".
3. **PRCH**: A larger blue rounded rectangle containing several yellow rounded rectangles. This block processes signals from "EDEC" and other control signals. The yellow rectangles within PRCH are:
\* "coherent combining"
\* "FD AGC"
\* "ZC correlation & IFFT"
\* "non-coherent combining"
\* "NPE & Peak Detection"
An arrow labeled "IQFP" connects "EDEC" to the "coherent combining" block within "PRCH".
4. **MDAB**: A blue rounded rectangle on the right, containing a yellow rounded rectangle labeled "Power measurements and reports". An arrow connects the "NPE & Peak Detection" block within "PRCH" to "MDAB".
Above the "PRCH" block, there are several oval-shaped control signals:
\* "fdAgcGain"
\* "prchScalingFactor"
\* "cohCombScale"

\* "nonCohCombScale"
\* "otherScales"

\* "fdAgcGain" points to "FD AGC".
\* "prchScalingFactor" points to "coherent combining" and "non-coherent combining".
\* "cohCombScale" points to "coherent combining".
\* "zcSeqCorrScale" points to "ZC correlation & IFFT".
\* "nonCohCombScale" points to "non-coherent combining".
\* "otherScales" points to "NPE & Peak Detection".
The overall flow starts from the "Radio Unit", goes through "EDEC" for decompression, then into the "PRCH" block for various signal processing steps, and finally to "MDAB" for power measurements and reporting. The control signals influence different stages of the "PRCH" processing.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2989.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3]

## 2.5.2 Power scaling parameters

### 2.5.2.1 Common parameters

#### 2.5.2.1.1 rxScalingFactor

**2.5.2.1.1.0-1**  (ID: `11418500`)

rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
11418500:
rxScalingFactor
Content of this requirement is frozen and valid until 23R3 release. For later releases please refer to the objects below

rxScalingFactor is a parameter that defines the RU receive gain. Intuitively, it is the smallest average signal power, at the RF input of the RU, expressed in tenths of dBm, that can be digitally handled by the gNB. A more accurate definition is that it is the average signal power, at the RF input of the RU, that gives rise, on the CPRI or eCPRI interface, to a signal with average (I²+Q²)  equal to 1 LSB. For CPRI, the average is taken over the time domain (over the I and Q samples of an OFDM symbol) with respect to the system full bandwidth whereas for eCPRI, the average is taken over the frequency domain (over the I and Q samples of an OFDM symbol) with respect to the bandwidth of one sub carrier as description in ORAN-WG4.CUS specification (Reference: [13349472](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_WBW7sOqoEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw?oslc_config.context=https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/gc/configuration/9)) chapter 6.1.3.2.2.

rxScalingFactor is common to all physical signals and channels. It needs to be known by the RU (since it sets its gain) and by L1-SW (since it is used to convert measurements performed by 5G-L1-UL and reported to 5G-L2-PS to mW or dBm). Care must be taken that the values of rxScalingFactor provided independently to the RU and to L1-SW are the same, otherwise power values reported by 5G-L1-UL to 5G-L2-PS will be incorrect.

In the CPRI case and OBSAI case, L1-SW uses the rxScalingFactor value provided by 5G-CP-RT in the UlCell\_SetupReq message (see [11513449: UlCell\_SetupReq message content](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRwhwfvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)).

**[CB006911-5G-A][CB007146-5G-A][CB007331-A][CB007331-B][CB007331-C][CB007149-A]**

rxScalingFactor from CP-RT is set per legacy wide carrier, here

for 30MHz, then value = -112.8 dBm

for **40MHz, the value = -112.8 dBm**

for 60MHz / 80MHz bandwidth , the value = -108 dBm

rxScalingFactor from NAHKA/legacy radio shall conform to -118.8 dBm per 30.72Msps (20MHz bandwidth) for each split carrier part.

So L1 UL shall ignore the value from CP-RT and use -118.8 dBm in carrier split cases and compensate the dB on ratio of normal FFT size to split FFT size since normal FFT size is used in section [11419907](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-fQhPvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) for simplicity as below formula, which is applied to traffic channels

[image-0][image\_desc]rxScalingFactor = 10 · (−118.8 + 10 · log₁₀(FFT\_ratio))[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2993.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.1.1-1)

while for PRACH channel, the PRB allocation does not get split across two carrier parts and no combination on frequency domain, then no FFT\_ratio compensation and the value of rxSclaingFactor shall be hardcoded to -118.8 dBm per either split carrier part.

Note that the unit of rxScalingFactor is 0.1 dB.

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a table with 7 rows and 5 columns. The table has a header row and then data rows organized into two main sections, FDD and TDD.
The columns are:
1. The first column is empty in the header row and contains "FDD" and "TDD" in the subsequent rows, indicating categories.
2. "BW (Sampling rate)"
3. "FFT size (Split mode)"
4. "FFT size (Normal mode)"
5. "FFT ratio (N/S)"
6. "compensation dB (=10\*LOG10(N/S))"
The table data is as follows:

| BW (Sampling rate) | FFT size (Split mode) | FFT size (Normal mode) | FFT ratio (N/S) | compensation dB (=10\*LOG10(N/S)) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 30MHz (2x 23.04 Msps) | 1536 | 3072 | 2 | 3 |
| 40MHz (2x 30.72 Msps) | 2048 | 4096 | 2 | 3 |
| 40MHz (2x 23.04 Msps) | 1536 | 3072 | 2 | 3 |
| 40MHz (2x 30.72 Msps) | 1024 | 2048 | 2 | 3 |
| 40MHz (2x 23.04 Msps) | 768 | 1536 | 2 | 3 |
| 60MHz (3x 30.72 Msps) | 1024 | 4096 | 4 | 6 |
| 80MHz (4x 30.72 Msps) | 1024 | 4096 | 4 | 6 |

**Note: Above description on split carrier cases is not applicable to ABIN, ASOE and ABIP.**

**[End CB006911-5G-A][End CB007146-5G-A][End CB007331-A][End CB007331-B][End CB007331-C][End CB007149-A]**

In the eCPRI case, with the introduction of CNI-55626 (5GC000399-S), L1-SW uses the new calculated rxScalingFactor  instead of default value -1520 (corresponding to -152 dBm), as stated in ORAN-WG4.CUS.0-v02.00.pdf chapter 6.1.3.2.2. Note that the range of values specified in  UlCell\_SetupReq ([11513449: UlCell\_SetupReq message content](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRwhwfvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) for rxScalingFactor, namely [-1300..-1000], is not adequate to convey value -1520, but this is not important since the value of rxScalingFactor in the UlCell\_SetupReq message is ignored in the eCPRI case. Regarding the calculation of rxScalingFactor, it shall be:

[image-2][image\_desc]The image contains the following text: rxScalingFactor = -1520 - gainCorrection[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2993.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2]    (equation 2.5.2.1.1-2)

[image-3][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in a blurry, sans-serif font. The equation reads:
`rxScalingFactorForPrach = -1520 - gainCorrectionForPrach`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_2993.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3]    (equation 2.5.2.1.1-3)

Where, gainCorrection and gainCorrectionForPrach with unit 0.1dB are taken from UlCell\_SetupReq ([11513449: UlCell\_SetupReq message content](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRwhwfvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)). Please note that the gainCorrection values depends on configured SCS and SCS for traffic channels and PRACH can be different so two values are taken and lead to separate rxScalingFactor for traffic channels and PRACH.

**[CB009443, CB009858-C] The requirement above for the eCPRI case  is applied to RINLINE1 L1 HW for FR1-FDD-eCPRI and FR1-TDD-eCPRI.** [End CB009443, CB009858-C]\*\*\*\*

**Note: ABIL only: L1-SW shall ignore gain\_correction when cni\_55626\_enabled is 0.**

**[5GC001053-A]**

Both gain\_corrections for non-PRACH and PRACH are also NIDD configurable in case of 14 bit mantissa. If the exponent range to received data is larger than 2, UL data will get distorted.

**[End 5GC001053-A]**

**[CB006844-5G-A]**

rxScalingFactor from CP-RT shall be -126.3 dBm for OBSAI radios. Exception is 900MHz RM variants, which uses -120.3 dBm.

**[End CB006844-5G-A]**

---

#### 2.5.2.1.2 rxScalingFactor for Loner only

##### 2.5.2.1.2.1 For CPRI

###### 2.5.2.1.2.1.1 Cell Setup

**2.5.2.1.2.1.1.0-2**  (ID: `11418530`)

Cell Setup
**For Loner CPRI case:**

L1-SW shall use the rxScalingFactor value provided by 5G-CP-RT (see 5G\_CP\_ARC\_ALG\_2450) in the UlCell\_SetupReq message ([11513449: UlCell\_SetupReq message content](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRwhwfvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)).

**[CNI-114758]**

**Note: For ASIR RRH radios which are not following CPRI L1L2 IDT specification, Radio shall report actual rxScalingFactor to OAM, then OAM forwards the value to CPlane, and CPlane forwards the value to L1-SW, the interface range defined in [11513449: UlCell\_SetupReq message content](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRwhwfvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) extends to [-1300,0] as radio can't specify the possbile range for all cases. However, there might be power measurements bias (e.g., noise power drift from thermal noise level ) based on reported rxScalingFactor. The variance is bigger with rxScalingFactor gets higher based on 5GMAX test vector verification, It is needed to double check with radio side on the reported rxScalingFactor when the error can't be neglected.**

**[End CNI-114758]**

---

###### 2.5.2.1.2.1.2 Cell reconfiguration

**2.5.2.1.2.1.2.0-1**  (ID: `11418540`)

Cell reconfiguration
**For Loner CPRI case:**

L1-SW shall update the rxScalingFactor value provided by 5G-CP-RT in the UlCell\_ParameterReconfigurationReq  message (see [11513565: UlCell\_ParameterReconfigurationReq](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRxv0vvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)).

**Note:**

For ASIR RRH radio NOT following CPRI L1L2 IDT specification, the radio shall report valid rxScalingFactor value to OAM only after cell activation, so it is necessary to have this cell reconfiguration message to pass through the valid value.

**For Loki CPRI split carriers case:**

rxScalingFactor from CP-RT is set per legacy wide carrier, here

for TDD and FDD 30MHz, then value = -112.8 dBm

for **TDD and FDD 40MHz, the value = -112.8 dBm**

for **TDD** [CB008935-A] and FDD **[End CB008935-A] 50MHz, the value = -112.8 dBm**\*\*\*\*

for 60MHz / 80MHz bandwidth , the value = -108 dBm

rxScalingFactor from NAHKA/legacy radio shall conform to -118.8 dBm per 30.72Msps (20MHz bandwidth) for each split carrier part.

So L1 UL shall ignore the value from CP-RT and use -118.8 dBm in carrier split cases and compensate the dB on ratio of normal FFT size to split FFT size since normal FFT size is used in section [11419907](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-fQhPvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) for simplicity as below formula, which is applied to traffic channels

[image-0][image\_desc]rxScalingFactor = 10 · (−118.8 + 10 · log₁₀(FFT\_ratio))[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3013.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.1.3-1)

while for PRACH channel, the PRB allocation does not get split across two carrier parts and no combination on frequency domain, then no FFT\_ratio compensation and the value of rxSclaingFactor shall be hardcoded to -118.8 dBm per either split carrier part.

Note that the unit of rxScalingFactor is 0.1 dB.

| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **BW (Sampling rate)** | **FFT size** (Split mode)\*\*\*\* | **FFT size** (Normal mode)\*\*\*\* | **FFT ratio** (N/S)\*\*\*\* | **compensation dB** (=10*LOG10(N/S))*\*\*\* | **First Feature Supported** |
| FR1-FDD | 30MHz (2x 23.04 Msps) | 1536 | 3072 (Note1) | 2 | 3 | CB007149-A |
| 40MHz (2x 30.72 Msps) | 2048 | 4096 | 2 | 3 | CB006991-A/CB007146-A |  |
| 40MHz (2x 23.04 Msps) | 1536 | 3072 | 2 | 3 | CB006991-A/CB007146-A |  |
| 50MHz (2x 30.72 Msps) | 2048 | 4096 | 2 | 3 | **CB008935-A** |  |
| FR1-TDD | 30MHz (2x 23.04 Msps) | 768 | 1536 (Note1) | 2 | 3 | CB009104-A |
| 40MHz (2x 30.72 Msps) | 1024 | 2048 | 2 | 3 | CB007331-A |  |
| 40MHz (2x 23.04 Msps) | 768 | 1536 | 2 | 3 | CB007331-A |  |
| 50MHz (2x 30.72 Msps) | 1204 | 2048 | 2 | 3 | CB009104-B |  |
| 60MHz (3x 30.72 Msps) | 1024 | 4096 | 4 | 6 | CB007331-B |  |
| 80MHz (4x 30.72 Msps) | 1024 | 4096 | 4 | 6 | CB007331-C |  |

**Note 1: End to end 30MHz sampling rate is 61.44Msps (See [11389682](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_r8M6kPvjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) and [11389715](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_sIMvMPvjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)), and 5GMAX pefers optimum 46.08Msps in split carrier case, so L1 UL PHY shall set ulActDownSampling as true irrespective any value received (see [11513477: CpriStaticConfig](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRxIw_vxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ))** and get corresponding FFT size after combination for power measurement purpose.\*\*\*\*

**Note 1:  Though the range of values specified in  UlCell\_SetupReq ([11513449: UlCell\_SetupReq message content](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRwhwfvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) for rxScalingFactor, namely [-1300..-1000], is not adequate to convey value -1520, this is not important since the value of rxScalingFactor in the UlCell\_SetupReq message is ignored in the eCPRI case.**

**Note 2:  the gainCorrection values depends on configured SCS and SCS for traffic channels and PRACH** can be different so two **values are taken and lead to separate rxScalingFactor for traffic channels and PRACH.**\*\*\*\*

**Note 3: [CB010765-A] A new term ru\_gain\_correct\_scs\_channel is introduced for gainCorrection calculation inside BOAM (Refer to [11689713: uplink gain correction calculation to L1H](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_nupg8PwjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)), and the new term value of NDM SRS could be different from the ones of traffic channels (Refer to [RadioModules.xlsx](https://nokia.sharepoint.com/:x:/r/sites/SM-RM_IDT/_layouts/15/Doc.aspx?sourcedoc=%7B4E2B81BF-F946-4234-B929-1FF2C6BA72AE%7D&file=RadioModules.xlsx&action=default&mobileredirect=true&DefaultItemOpen=1) for each channel's value definition per Radio family), so a separate rxScalingFactorForNdmSrs needs to be calculated.** [End CB010765-A]\*\*\*\*

**Note 4: Both gain\_corrections for non-PRACH and PRACH are also NIDD configurable in case of 14 bit mantissa. If the exponent range to received data is larger than 2, UL data will get distorted.**

---

#### 2.5.2.1.4 rxScalingFactor for Thor only

##### 2.5.2.1.4.1 For CPRI Normal carrier and OBSAI

###### 2.5.2.1.4.1.1 Cell Setup

**2.5.2.1.4.1.1.0-2**  (ID: `11418695`)

Cell Setup
**For Thor CPRI normal and OBSAI case:**

L1-SW shall use the rxScalingFactor value provided by 5G-CP-RT (see [11288559: UlCell\_SetupReq](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_wYAN8PvXEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) in the UlCell\_SetupReq message (see [11513449: UlCell\_SetupReq message content](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRwhwfvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)).

**[CNI-114758]**

**Note: For ASIR RRH radios which are not following CPRI L1L2 IDT specification, Radio shall report actual rxScalingFactor to OAM, then OAM forwards the value to CPlane, and CPlane forwards the value to L1-SW, the interface range defined in [11513449: UlCell\_SetupReq message content](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRwhwfvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) extends to [-1300,0] as radio can't specify the possbile range for all cases. However, there might be power measurements bias (e.g., noise power drift from thermal noise level ) based on reported rxScalingFactor. The variance is bigger with rxScalingFactor gets higher based on 5GMAX test vector verification, It is needed to double check with radio side on the reported rxScalingFactor when the error can't be neglected.**

**[End CNI-114758]**

---

###### 2.5.2.1.4.1.2 Cell Reconfiguration

**2.5.2.1.4.1.2.0-1**  (ID: `11418707`)

Cell Reconfiguration
**For Thor CPRI normal case:**

L1-SW shall update the rxScalingFactor value provided by 5G-CP-RT in the UlCell\_ParameterReconfigurationReq  message (see [11513565: UlCell\_ParameterReconfigurationReq](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRxv0vvxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)).

**Note:**

For ASIR RRH radio NOT following CPRI L1L2 IDT specification, the radio shall report valid rxScalingFactor value to OAM only after cell activation, so it is necessary to have this cell reconfiguration message to pass through the valid value.

##### 2.5.2.1.4.2 For CPRI Split carrier

**2.5.2.1.4.2.0-3**  (ID: `11418744`)

For CPRI Split carrier

11418744:
For CPRI Split carrier
11418744:
For CPRI Split carrier
11418744:
For CPRI Split carrier
**For Thor CPRI split carriers case:**

rxScalingFactor from CP-RT is set per legacy wide carrier, here

For FDD 40MHz, value = -112.8 dBm;

For FDD 30MHz, value = -112.8 dBm;

**[CB008935-A] For FDD 50MHz, value = -112.8 dBm;** [End CB008935-A]\*\*\*\*

rxScalingFactor from NAHKA/legacy radio shall conform to -118.8 dBm per 30.72Msps (20MHz bandwidth) for each split carrier part.

So L1 UL shall ignore the value from CP-RT and use -118.8 dBm in carrier split cases and compensate the dB on ratio of **unnormalized FFT size to split FFT size since normal FFT size is used in section [11420081](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-fQi_vvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) for simplicity as below formula, which is applied to traffic channels**

[image-0][image\_desc]rxScalingFactor = 10 · (−118.8 + 20 · log₁₀(FFT\_ratio))[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3027.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.1.4-1)

while for PRACH channel, the PRB allocation does not get split across two carrier parts and no combination on frequency domain, then no FFT\_ratio compensation and the value of rxSclaingFactor shall be hardcoded to -118.8 dBm per either split carrier part.

Note that the unit of rxScalingFactor is 0.1 dB.

|  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **BW (Sampling rate)** | **FFT size** (Split mode)\*\*\*\* | **FFT size** (Normal mode)\*\*\*\* | **FFT ratio** (N/S)\*\*\*\* | **compensation dB** (=20*LOG10(N/S))*\*\*\* | **First Feature Supported** |
| FR1-FDD | 30MHz (2x 23.04 Msps) | 1536 | 3072 (Note 1) | 2 | 6 | CB009028: Parity from CB007149 |
| 40MHz (2x 30.72 Msps) | 2048 | 4096 | 2 | 6 | RP003187: Parity from CB007146 |  |
| 50MHz (2x 30.72 Msps) | 2048 | 4096 | 2 | 6 | **CB008935-A** |  |

**Note 1: End to end 30MHz sampling rate is 61.44Msps (See [11389682](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_r8M6kPvjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) and [11389715](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_sIMvMPvjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)), and 5GMAX prefers optimum 46.08Msps in split carrier case, so L1 UL PHY shall set ulActDownSampling as true irrespective any value received (see [11513477: CpriStaticConfig](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_FRxIw_vxEe-AqvopbP1qhQ))** and get corresponding FFT size for combination.\*\*\*\*

Note 4: rxScalingFactorForNdmSrs is not used in TDD FR2 as NDM SRS is not supported in TDD FR2.

### 2.5.2.2 Parameters for Loner only

#### 2.5.2.2.1 decimationFactor

##### 2.5.2.2.1.0-1 decimationFactor decimationFactor is gain of the decimation filter for PRACH in CPRI chain. It depends on the coefficients. For long format, decimationFactor = 1.7 and for short format, decimationFactor = 1.0 (no filter). For eCPRI case, decimationFactor = 1.0 for both long format and short format. (ID: 11418816)

#### 2.5.2.2.2 fftScalingFactor

**2.5.2.2.2.0-1**  (ID: `11418835`)

fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
11418835:
fftScalingFactor
Since unnormalized FFT form is used from 5G20B onwards, the power in frequency domain shall be scaled up to NFFT times of the one in time domain, then L1SW needs to rescale this down in measurements computation, the formula is written in section [11419837](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-epgPvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) chapter 6.6.5.1 in detail. Please be noted this scaling factor is only applied to traffic channels and signals except for PRACH which has other formula to include this as one coefficient for convention.

unnormalized FFT form in use: [image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula. The formula is for the Discrete Fourier Transform (DFT). It is written as:
$X(k) = \sum\_{n=0}^{N\_{FFT}-1} x(n) \cdot e^{-j \frac{2\pi nk}{N\_{FFT}}}$
Where:
- $X(k)$ is the DFT of the sequence $x(n)$.
- $x(n)$ is the input sequence.
- $N\_{FFT}$ is the number of points in the DFT.
- $n$ is the index of the input sequence.
- $k$ is the index of the DFT output.
- $j$ is the imaginary unit.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3036.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.2.2-1)

Power conservation rule (Parseval’s theorem): [image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation states that the sum of the squared magnitudes of a discrete-time signal $x(n)$ from $n=0$ to $N\_{FFT}-1$ is equal to $\frac{1}{N\_{FFT}}$ times the sum of the squared magnitudes of its Discrete Fourier Transform $X(k)$ from $k=0$ to $N\_{FFT}-1$. This is known as Parseval's theorem for the Discrete Fourier Transform.
The equation is written as:
$$ \sum\_{n=0}^{N\_{FFT}-1} |x(n)|^2 = \frac{1}{N\_{FFT}} \sum\_{k=0}^{N\_{FFT}-1} |X(k)|^2 $$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3036.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.2.2-2)

---

11418853:
postFftScalingFactor
This factor is only introduced in the PRACH TDD CPRI case, for both long PRACH formats (FFT size is fixed and equal to 1536) and short PRACH formats (FFT size is same as traffic channel), since L1 FPGA implements non fully compensation on unnormalized FFT with one right shift which equal to floor of logarithm two of NFFT, then L1SW needs to recompensate this for those cases that NFFT doesn’t equal to an even power of two to achieve normalized FFT form. And the values are as follows:

 postFftScalingFactor = 1 for CPRI when NFFT is an even power of 2;

 postFftScalingFactor = 1 / sqrt (2) for CPRI when NFFT is an odd power of 2;

 postFftScalingFactor = sqrt (2/3) for CPRI when NFFT is equal to 3 multiplying by an odd power of 2 (e.g., 1536 = 3.29);

 postFftScalingFactor = 1 / sqrt (3) for CPRI when NFFT is equal to 3 multiplying by an even power of 2 (e.g., 768 = 3.28 and 3072 = 3. 210);

 postFftScalingFactor = 1 for eCPRI in all cases. (The parameter will be also used in the formulas for the PRACH TDD eCPRI case to have common formulas for both CPRI and eCPRI.)

normalized FFT form in use: [image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula. The formula is for the Discrete Fourier Transform (DFT). It is written as:
$X(k) = \frac{1}{\sqrt{N\_{FFT}}} \sum\_{n=0}^{N\_{FFT}-1} x(n) \cdot e^{-j \frac{2\pi nk}{N\_{FFT}}}$
Where:
- $X(k)$ represents the DFT of the signal $x(n)$ at frequency bin $k$.
- $N\_{FFT}$ is the number of points in the Fast Fourier Transform.
- $x(n)$ is the input signal in the time domain.
- $n$ is the time index.
- $k$ is the frequency index.
- $j$ is the imaginary unit.
- $e$ is the base of the natural logarithm.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3038.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.2.3-1)

Power conservation rule (Parseval’s theorem): [image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation states that the sum of the squared magnitudes of a sequence $x(n)$ from $n=0$ to $N\_{FFT}-1$ is equal to the sum of the squared magnitudes of its Discrete Fourier Transform $X(k)$ from $k=0$ to $N\_{FFT}-1$. This is known as Parseval's theorem for discrete-time signals.
The equation is written as:
$$ \sum\_{n=0}^{N\_{FFT}-1} |x(n)|^2 = \sum\_{k=0}^{N\_{FFT}-1} |X(k)|^2 $$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3038.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.2.3-2)

---

According to IFFT power chapter  of 5G\_Algorithm\_Specification\_PRACH\_fixed\_point\_22R3 (Reference: [13349507](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_V75TQOqwEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), the calculated power has deviation from the one achieved by normalized IFFT form (the 1st row in Table of Reference [11417042](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-URb_vvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)), then L1SW needs to recompensate this with postIfftScalingFactor and the value is calculated as follow:

#### 2.5.2.2.5 max_shift and ant_shift

**2.5.2.2.5.0-1**  (ID: `11418914`)

max\_shift and ant\_shift
11418914:

11418914:

11418914:

11418914:
max\_shift and ant\_shift
11418914:
max\_shift and ant\_shift
11418914:
max\_shift and ant\_shift
According to AGC post-FFT chapter of PRACH FXP algorithm specification, TDD PRACH shall apply AGC on the data per logical antenna in order to adjust the range for the fixed point. And the fraction bits from both input data and output data of AGC module are 14 bits, so for PRACH there is no additional scaling coming from fix point to floating point conversion. The only concern is the AGC shift itself.

Furthermore, as stated in non-coherent combining chapter, it shall be considered the scaling per logic antenna which could have been different due to the AGC, then the antenna wise AGC shift shall be revised and max shift value among all antennas shall be selected as the common scaling on all antennas. Please be noted that antenna wise AGC shift is applied on amplitude and the max\_shift (= 2\*maxAgcShift) is applied on power.

Moreover, cumulated power of all logical antennas is calculated and additional ant\_shift is added in order to compensate the value increase due to antenna combination. Then the overall scaling factor of both post-FFT AGC and non-coherent combining steps is calculated as follow to get the antenna wise output

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is:
$2^{-\frac{\text{max\_shift}}{2}} \cdot \sqrt{\frac{N\_L}{2^{\text{ant\_shift}}}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3042.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.2.5-1)

Where,

max\_shift shall be given to L1SW from FPGA by rx\_status measurements output;

mPower\_shift depends on the number of logical antenna (NL) with below table:

|  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| NL | 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 6 | 8 | 12 | 16 |
| ant\_shift | 0 | 1 | 2 | 2 | 3 | 3 | 4 | 4 |

And

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in black text on a white background. The equation is:
$N\_L = N\_{RX} \cdot N\_{RA}^{symb}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3042.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.2.5-2)

[image-2][image\_desc]The image contains the text "NRx" in a stylized font. The letters are colored with a gradient of orange, yellow, and blue, and have a black outline. The text is slightly blurry.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3042.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2] = 2 in case of 2 RX receiver and [image-3][image\_desc]The image contains the text "NRx" in a stylized font. #### 2.5.2.2.6 agcShiftChannelType

**2.5.2.2.6.0-1**  (ID: `11418930`)

agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:

agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
11418930:
agcShiftChannelType
This parameter allows to perform post-FFT AGC on the physical signal or channel identified by ChannelType. It is a right shift by a certain number of bits to reduce the bitwidth from 25 bits (Q 1.10.14) to 12 bits (Q1.0.11). The number of bits to be shifted is specific to one UE and dynamically determined based on signal amplitude computation. The signal amplitude computation is performed on all RB allocated the UE and all receive antennas. This amplitude computation is to be performed on the first allocated OFDM symbol of the slot. Depending on the most significant bit detected on the highest computed amplitude, deduce the shift to apply so that this signal can be reduced to 12 bits.

This factor is used for PUSCH (agcShiftPusch), PUCCH (agcShiftPucch) and SRS (agcShiftSrs). L1 FPGA shall provide the value of each specific channel or signal to L1SW, then the scaling factor during this stage is as follow formula

[image-0][image\_desc]2(3-agcShiftChannelType)[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3044.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.2.6-1)

Please note that agcShiftChannelType itself is a signed value, when it is a negative value, a left shift is performed to boost signal amplitude for low SNR UEs and small FFT sizes. Additionally, the value 3 is coming from input data fraction bits 14 minus output data fraction bits 11 because the real value (floating point) is used in this document as stated in section 8.2.

---

#### 2.5.2.2.7 alphaAgcChannelType

**2.5.2.2.7.0-1**  (ID: `11418941`)

alphaAgcChannelType
An extra coefficient alphaAgcChannelType is used to take advantage of the full dynamic of the 12 bits.

A margin of 1 bit can eventually be added to the shift value to accommodate the maximum amplitude difference between DMRS and data symbols. This margin and the scaling value of alphaAgcPusch depend on the following parameters:

1) whether transform precoding is activated,

2) whether AGC shift is computed on a DMRS or data symbol,

3) whether DMRS is boosted,

4) PUSCH traffic modulation.

In case of transform precoding, the margin bit is set to 1 and there is no additional scaling, i.e. the scaling value is 1.

In case of no transform precoding, the values of margin bit and the scaling are given in below table.

|  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| First Symbol | DMRS boost | PUSCH modulation | Amplitude ratio between data and DMRS | Margin | Scaling |
| Data | 0 dB | QPSK | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| Data | 0 dB | 16-QAM | 3/sqrt (5) | 0 | 1 |
| Data | 0 dB | 64-QAM | sqrt (7/3) | 0 | 1 |
| Data | 3 dB | QPSK | sqrt (1/2) | 1 | sqrt (2) |
| Data | 3 dB | 16-QAM | 3 / sqrt (10) | 1 | 6 / sqrt (10) |
| Data | 3 dB | 64-QAM | sqrt (7/6) | 0 | 1 |
| DMRS | 0 dB | QPSK | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| DMRS | 0 dB | 16-QAM | 3/sqrt (5) | 1 | 2\*sqrt (5)/3 |
| DMRS | 0 dB | 64-QAM | sqrt (7/3) | 1 | 2\*sqrt (3/7) |
| DMRS | 3 dB | QPSK | sqrt (1/2) | 0 | 1 |
| DMRS | 3 dB | 16-QAM | 3 / sqrt (10) | 0 | 1 |
| DMRS | 3 dB | 64-QAM | sqrt (7/6) | 1 | 2\*sqrt (6/7) |

Table‑1: Margin and AGC scaling values

Note that for all other channels or signals than PUSCH, margin is set to 0 and scaling to 1. So alphaAgcPucch and alphaAgcSrs are equal to 1.

---

#### 2.5.2.2.8 xScale

##### 2.5.2.2.8.0-1 xScale TOC module in L1 FPGA shall use xScale to reduce the signal amplitude so that no overflow beyond 12 bits is experienced at the output of the remaining processing blocks of the receiver. In the current working view, xScale is equal to 0.5 but could be further optimized. (ID: 11418954)

#### 2.5.2.2.9 shift

**2.5.2.2.9.0-1**  (ID: `11418966`)

shift
In case of eCPRI interface, first there shall be a sign extension operation by (29 -WL) during eCPRI decompression stage to be applied to the mantissa, where WL is the mantissa size (WL = 14 or 9, other values are not supported).

Then a left shift by (exponent + leftShift) and a reduction to Q (1.10.14) format is applied. Here, exponent is the exponent value over eCPRI for the PRB being processed, with values in the range [0,15]. leftShift is an additional parameter that can be used to set the receiver dynamic range or correct potential design errors.

The default value of leftShift = 14 guarantees that the LSB of the Q (1.10.14) format at the output of the IQ decompression stage corresponds to a power level of rxScalingFactor (-152 dBm).

In the sequel we will use a parameter shift defined as (14 – leftShift) which corresponds to a deviation from the default value of 14 and to a right shift. The default value of shift is 0. Hence having shift set to 0 amounts to performing no scaling at all.

shift will appear in the Rx power scaling formulas for the various physical signals and channels (provided in chapters 5.6.5 below). The default value of shift is 0. In order to have the same formulas for eCPRI and CPRI, shift will be also used in the formulas for the CPRI case, but its value will always be 0.

---

#### 2.5.2.2.10 Summary of the power scaling parameters

**2.5.2.2.10.0-1**  (ID: `11418977`)

Summary of the power scaling parameters
The various parameters introduced above are gathered in the following table along with a short description. “Common” in the table means that the parameter applies to all physical signals and channels.

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Scaling parameters | PUSCH | PUCCH | PRACH | SRS |
| rxScalingFactor (pre-FFT) | Common Configured | Common Configured | Common Configured | Common Configured |
| decimationFactor | Not applicable | Not applicable | Long format: 1.8 (TDD CPRI) 1.0 otherwise | Not applicable |
| fftScalingFactor | Common Configured | Common Configured | Not applicable | Common Configured |
| postFftScalingFactor (post-FFT), used for the implementation of the unitary form of the FFT in the PRACH TDD CPRI only case, not relevant for eCPRI where it is set to 1 | Not applicable | Not applicable | 1/sqrt(2) when NFFT is an odd power of 2, sqrt(2/3) when NFFT = 1536, 1/sqrt(3) when NFFT = 768 or 3072, 1 otherwise | Not applicable |
| postIfftScalingFactor, used for the implementation of the unitary form of the IFFT in the PRACH TDD case. | Not applicable | Not applicable | calculated | Not applicable |
| max\_shift | Not applicable | Not applicable | max\_shift | Not applicable |
| ant\_shift | Not applicable | Not applicable | ant\_shift | Not applicable |
| agcShfitChannelType | agcShiftPusch | agcShiftPucch | Not applicable | agcShiftSrs |
| alphaAgcChannelType | alphaAgcPusch | alphaAgcPucch set to 1 | Not applicable | alphaAgcSrs set to 1 |
| xScale | Common Const 0.5 | Common Const 0.5 | Not applicable | Common Const 0.5 |
| shift (relevant only for eCPRI, provision for design errors, set to 0 for CPRI) | Common | Common | Common | Common |

### 2.5.2.3 Parameters for Loki only

#### 2.5.2.3.1 inputGainChannelType

**2.5.2.3.1.0-4**  (ID: `11419010`)

inputGainChannelType
InputGainChannelType is a generic name that stands for inputGainPusch, inputGainPucch, or inputGainSrs , depending on the considered physical channel or signal.

For the CPRI case, inputGainChannelType in ULFE ISS block performs a scaling at the input of the FFT for the particular channel or signal of interest in order to prevent unwanted distortion or underflow within the FFT calculation and the other processing blocks in the ULFE signal chain. The way inputGainChannelType is calculated is explained in Reference: [13349496](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_creYYeqqEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw) § 19.1.4. The gain is calculated to adjust the current input signal level to the target level, which can be set by ULFE normal job configuration. This calculation can be performed on the first OFDM symbol when ISS\_MODE is set to 0x1 in the job of first symbol and applied the fixed gain to other symbols belonging to the signal or channel in the slot when ISS\_MODE is set to 0x0 in the job of other symbols. it can be also performed to all the OFDM symbols with ISS\_MODE = 0x1 in all jobs.

L1 adopts the later configuration with ISS\_MODE = 0x1 for all the OFDM symbols and based on all simulation results, ISS\_TARGET\_LEVEL = 19 is recommended and applicable for all cases. Then ISS block shall output one 3-dB-step gain G and inputGainChannelType is calculated with 2^(G/2).

According to Reference: [13349496](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_creYYeqqEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw) § 19.1.5, in ISS block, the signal level is up or down scaled in order to avoid unwanted saturation and to maximize the signal quality through FFT. Because the FFT engine in ULFE has no signal gain, the signal level can be normalized to adjust the whole signal gain in ULFE to 0 dB. Signal level normalization block is a reverse function of the signal scaler and requires the scaling gain which is calculated in ISS block. The normalization shall be turned off from 5G20B onwards by configuring the bit of SIGNAL\_LEVEL\_NORMALIZE to 0 in ULFE\_NORMAL\_JOB\_S.

Above requirement support based on technology as below table:

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Loki** |
| FR1-FDD-OBSAI | supported |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported |
| FR1-TDD-CPRI | supported |
| FR2-TDD-CPRI | - |

With carrier split mode (FDD 30MHz **[Before CB008935-A] and 40MHz** [CB008935-A], 40MHz and 50MHz **[End CB008935-A], TDD 30MHz, 50MHz, 40Mhz, 60MHz and 80MHz), two or more (up to four) ULFE jobs per antenna per symbol are used in parallel and there are multiple ISS gains output per antenna per symbol from ULFE according to number of splits (e.g., 2 ISS gains with 2 splits, 3 ISS gains with 3 splits), current algorithm is to calculate one single gain with multiple outputs with refer to 5GMAX proposal, then perform rescaling on IQ samples in FD FOC step and use the calculated gain for later FDEQ processing and power measurements.**\*\*\*\*

**Note: Above description on split cases is not applicable to ABIN and ASOE.**

For the eCPRI case, this parameter is not relevant since the FFT is performed in the RU and no AGC is performed within the RU.

Based on above description, the inputGainChannelType shall appear in the Rx power calculations performed by L1-SW.

---

#### 2.5.2.3.2 fftScalingFactor

**2.5.2.3.2.0-2**  (ID: `11419026`)

fftScalingFactor
From the ULFE description on FFT engine without signal gain, it is concluded that the unitary version of the FFT is implemented, so that FFT preserves power. The other FFT performed in PRCH or MDAB later shall also follow this. So the parameter fftScalingFactor is equal to 1 and does not appear in the Rx power calculations performed by L1-SW.

Above requirement support based on technology and HW board as below table:

| **Technology** | **ABIO** | **ABIN** | **ASOE** | **ASOF** | **RINLINE1** |
| FR1-FDD-OBSAI | supported | supported | supported | - | - |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported | supported | supported | **[CB009223-C] supported** [End CB009223-C]\*\*\*\* | supported |
| FR1-TDD-CPRI | supported | - | supported | **[CB009223-D] supported** [End CB009223-D]\*\*\*\* | supported |
| FR2-TDD-CPRI | - | - | - | - | - |

#### 2.5.2.3.3 prachTimeAgcGain

**2.5.2.3.3.0-2**  (ID: `11419044`)

prachTimeAgcGain
According to Reference: [13349496](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_creYYeqqEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw) § 18.1.2, the T-AGC module in PRCH accumulates the last 512 samples (regardless of preamble format) of the symbol and calculates the average power and this value is used to control the target signal power for all input samples before feeding them to the FFT block.

The target signal power is controlled by L1-SW with T-AGC back-off value such that

Target Signal Power = 3 dB x (31-TAGC\_BACKOFF)

For example, if the T-AGC back-off value is 11, T-AGC sets the target signal power to 60 dB (corresponding to an RMS of 210).

Based on target signal power and the measured signal power of the last 512 samples, the T-AGC block calculates gains and adjusts scaling of input samples as s*out = ( G*scale / 2*Gexp ) x s*in\*\*\*\*

The scaling factors are reported in the write DMA report as

AGC\_CONTROL\_VALUE\_ANTn = 29 x G*exp + G*scale\*\*

Where:

n is the antenna number

G*exp is represented as the 4 MSBs*

G*scale is represented as 9 LSBs*

So prachTimeAgcGain is a linear value that equal to G*scale / 2*Gexp .\*\*

Above requirement support based on technology and HW board as below table:

|  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **ABIO** | **ABIN** | **ASOE** | **ASOF** | **RINLINE1** |
| FR1-FDD-OBSAI | supported | supported | supported | - | - |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported | supported | supported | **[CB009223-C] supported** [End CB009223-C]\*\*\*\* | supported |
| FR1-TDD-CPRI | supported | - | supported | **[CB009223-D] supported** [End CB009223-D]\*\*\*\* | supported |
| FR2-TDD-CPRI | - | - | - | - |  |

RINLINE 1 support is terminated in 24R1, requirement is not valid for RINLINE 1 starting from 24R2.

---

11419128:
prchScalingFactor
With PRACH channel specific processing of ZC sequence correlation and antenna coherent combine, two separate factors zcCorrScale and cohCombScale shall contribute the power scaling and they are calculated as below formulas:

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is written in a light gray font on a white background. The equation reads:
zcCorrScale = $\sqrt{\frac{L\_{RA}}{N\_{IFFT}}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3067.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.3.4-1)

where here NIFFT = 512 for PRACH short formats with preamble length LRA = 139 and NIFFT = 2048 for PRACH long formats with preamble length LRA = 839.

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in a light blue font against a white background. The equation is:
`cohCombScale = cohCombLen · s_coh · 2^-(b_coh+8)`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3067.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.3.4-2)

Where here[image-2][image\_desc]The image contains the text "cohCombLen" in a light gray, italicized font. The text is positioned at the bottom of the image, against a white background.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3067.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2] is the actual coherent combing length, b\_coh and s\_coh are from 5GMAX code (CohCombTable) and can be selected according to configuration of N\_COH in PRACH\_JD\_SYS\_CFG\_S, which determines how many symbols are coherently combined before computing the PRACH power.

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| N\_COH | Combined symbols | b\_coh | s\_coh |
| 0 | 1 | 0 | 256 |
| 1 | 2 | 1 | 362 |
| 2 | 3 | 1 | 296 |
| 3 | 4 | 1 | 256 |
| 4 | 6 | 1 | 209 |
| 5 | 8 | 2 | 362 |
| 6 | 12 | 2 | 296 |
| 7 | 24 | 2 | 209 |

Table-3: CohComhTable parameters

According to Marvell’s guidance, there is scaling down by 10 bits for 839 ZC length and 9 bits for 139 ZC length, so

With preamble length LRA = 839

[image-3][image\_desc]The image contains the text "scalePerAnt = 2⁻⁵". The text is in a light gray color against a white background. The font appears to be a serif font. The exponent "-5" is smaller and raised above the base "2".[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3067.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3]    (equation 2.5.2.3.4-3)

With preamble length LRA = 139

[image-4][image\_desc]The image contains the text "scalePerAnt = 2⁻⁴·⁵". The text is in a light gray color against a white background. The font appears to be a serif font. The text is horizontally aligned and centered within the image.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3067.005.png[/image\_path][/image-4]    (equation 2.5.2.3.4-4)

The final power profile from PRCH output is taking the power contribution from multiple RX antennas in, to keep consistent with 5GMAX, the contribution shall be considered as power scaling  to be rescaled  via square root of number of ative antennas, also the power profile output is integer value, then the floating point input conversion is to be considered via

[image-5][image\_desc]convScale = 15[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3067.006.png[/image\_path][/image-5]

For both CPRI case and eCPRI case

So final prchScalingFactor shall be calculated as

[image-6][image\_desc]prchScalingFactor = convScale · zcCorrScale · cohCombScale · scalePerAnt · $\sqrt{numAntComb}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3067.007.png[/image\_path][/image-6]    (equation 2.5.2.3.4-5)

| FR1-FDD-OBSAI | supported | supported | supported | - | - |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported | supported | supported | **[CB009223-C] supported** [End CB009223-C]\*\*\*\* | - |

The decimation chain is implemented to perform reduced size FFT, and decimateScalingFactor shall be calculated as

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula. The formula is for "decimateScalingFactor" and is expressed as:
decimateScalingFactor = $\frac{(DecimRatio0)^5 \cdot 2^{-(OutputLevelAtten0)}}{\sqrt{(DecimRatio0) \cdot (2^{(OversampleRatio0)})}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.3.5-1)

Where here OversampleRatio0, DecimRatio0 and OutputLevelAtten0 are parameters configured in ULFE\_NORMAL\_JOB\_S. Below paragraph explains how to calculate the parameters to be configured.

Assuming FFTLength is the parameter configured according to the cell’s sampling rate per different bandwidth, FFTSizeDec is the parameter configured per the request of PRCH handling (2048 for long format and 512 for short format), and FFTSize is the least common multiple of the FFTLength and FFTSizeDec, then

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a single line of text in a serif font. The text reads: "DecimRatio0 = FFTSize / FFTSizeDec".[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.3.5-2)

[image-2][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is: OversampleRatio0 = log₂(FFTSize / FFTLength). The text is in a light gray color and is italicized. The equation is centered horizontally in the image.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2]    (equation 2.5.2.3.5-3)

If [image-3][image\_desc]The image contains the text "DecimRatio0" in a light gray, italicized font. The text is positioned at the bottom of the image against a white background.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3] is larger than 1 (the range of [image-4][image\_desc]The image contains the text "DecimRatio0" in a light gray color against a white background. The text is in a serif font and appears to be slightly italicized.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.005.png[/image\_path][/image-4]is from 2 to 48), then

[image-5][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray font on a white background. The formula is:

The formula appears to be a definition or calculation for a variable named "OutputLevelAtten0". It involves rounding a calculation that includes a logarithm base 2, a division, and a multiplication.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.006.png[/image\_path][/image-5]    (equation 2.5.2.3.5-4)

Else

#### 2.5.2.3.6 nShift

**2.5.2.3.6.0-2**  (ID: `11419234`)

nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:

11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
11419234:
nShift
Frequency domain dynamic scaling is introduced for eCPRI case after RE-demapping to scale all the demapped IQ samples to certain level for all UL physical channels and provide enough precision for remaing processing in the UL data path without performance loss. The algorithm is to calculate shift factor “nShift” equal to delta between target and MSB as below (Reference: [13349510](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_uzm14Oq_EfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)).

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray font on a white background. The formula is:
`nShift = xTarget - length(dec2bin(2^Q_IQ-in * max(|I|, |Q|))) antenna wise, one OFDM symbol`
The formula appears to be related to signal processing, possibly in the context of wireless communications or digital signal processing. Specifically, it defines a variable `nShift` in terms of `xTarget`, the length of a binary representation of a calculated value, and some parameters like `Q_IQ-in`, `I`, and `Q`. The terms "antenna wise" and "OFDM symbol" suggest its application in a multi-antenna Orthogonal Frequency-Division Multiplexing system.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3073.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.3.6-1)

where,

I/Q are samples of the OFDM symbols for the corresponding UL physical channels of a specific UE per antenna wise and I/Q Q format depends on definition of each traffic channel.

xTarget is a predefined target value. Current proposed value is 12 with 3 bits margin and may be further tuned by fixed point based performance evaluation.

Left shift when nShift is positive value, and right shift when nShift is negative value, so the scaling factor is equal to

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains the mathematical expression "2^n.shift". The text is in a light blue color and is slightly blurry. The exponent "n.shift" is smaller than the base "2" and is positioned above and to the right of it.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3073.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.3.6-2)

More channel specific details are written in section [11420635](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-geqPvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ).

Above requirement support based on technology and HW board as below table:

|  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **ABIO** | **ABIN** | **ASOE** | **ASOF** | **RINLINE1** |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | - | - | supported |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | supported | supported | **[CB009223-B] supported** [End CB009223-B]\*\*\*\* | supported |
| FR2-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | - | - | - |

RINLINE 1 support is terminated in 24R1, requirement is not valid for RINLINE 1 starting from 24R2.

#### 2.5.2.3.7 fdAgcGain

**2.5.2.3.7.0-2**  (ID: `11419288`)

fdAgcGain
11419288:

11419288:
fdAgcGain
Loki PRCH performs frequency domain automatic gain control after demapping. This function can be enabled with FDAGC\_ON of PRCH\_JOB\_CFG\_S.

When FDAGC\_ON = 0, then fdAgcGain = 1;

When FDAGC\_ON = 1, then fdAgcGain calculation depends on FREQ\_BYPASS setting of PRACH\_JD\_CAL\_PARM\_S.

When FREQ\_BYPASS = 1 (eCPRI case), Loki PRACH gets FD samples input. The targeted signal power at the output of FD-AGC is controlled by software with a back-off value specified in FDAGC\_BACKOFF of PRCH\_JOB\_CFG\_S, such that FDAGC\_BACKOFF is set to 12 per 5GMAX proposal, then

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is:
$f d A g c G a i n = 2^{\frac{31 - 2 \cdot ConvScal - \log 2(\text{Target Power}) - FDAGC\_BACKOFF}{2}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3076.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.3.7-1)

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains the text "Target Power" in a light gray color against a white background. The text is slightly blurry.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3076.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1] is the mean power over all repetition symbols and antennas.

[image-2][image\_desc]ConvScal[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3076.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2] = 15, which represents the number of fractional bits of eCPRI case.

When FREQ\_BYPASS = 0 (CPRI case), Loki PRACH gets TD samples input, then according the 5GMAX algorithm

[image-3][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is:
$f dAgcGain = 2^{\frac{TAGC\_BACKOFF-FDAGC\_BACKOFF-1}{2}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3076.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3]     (equation 2.5.2.3.7-2)

TAGC\_BACKOFF is set to 12 per 5GMAX proposal.

**[CB012261-A] In LOKI, the conditions in which FDAGC is on or off are described in [11449596](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_fAFzAPvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ).** [End CB012261-A]\*\*\*\*

|  |  |
| --- | --- |

| FR1-FDD-OBSAI | supported |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported |
| FR1-FDD-eCPRI | supported |

fftScalingFactor
11419330:
fftScalingFactor
ULFE in Thor uses unnormalized FFT form,  the power in frequency domain shall be scaled up to NFFT times of the one in time domain, then L1SW needs to rescale this down in measurements computation via fftScalingFactor, which is equivalent to Spost defined in 5GMAX specification. This fftScalingFactor is applicable to all uplink channels including PRACH, which uses ULFE to perform FFT after sample rate conversion since no FFT in PRCH in Thor, and PRACH FFT size can be different from the one used for traffic channel, it depends on PRACH format  and same as PRACH IFFT size, so to differentiate the two:

For traffic channel:

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in a light gray font against a white background. The equation reads:
`fftScalingFactor = sqrt(N_FFT)`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3081.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.4.1-1)

where, [image-1][image\_desc]The image contains the text "NFFT" in a light blue, serif font. The text is positioned in the bottom left corner of the image.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3081.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1] depends on BW and sampling rate.

For PRACH:

[image-2][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in a light gray font against a white background. The equation reads:
`fftScalingFactor = sqrt(N_IFFT)`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3081.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2]    (equation 2.5.2.4.1-2)

where here [image-3][image\_desc]The image contains the text "N IFFT" in a blue font. The text is slightly blurry.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3081.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3] = 512 for PRACH short formats with preamble length LRA = 139 and NIFFT = 2048 for PRACH long formats with preamble length LRA = 839

#### 2.5.2.4.2 comExp

**2.5.2.4.2.0-3**  (ID: `11419356`)

comExp
SDEC in Thor is used to decompress data in IQFP format and coverts it into eFXP format per each PRB group, and each sample in eFXP format is composed of a 16-bit mantissa for I and Q and groups of samples share one exponent. Then 16-bit mantissa after SDEC is used in subsequent data path of traffic channel without shared exponent in data processing, so L1SW needs to rescale this in measurements computation via 2^(-comExp). This comExp is applicable to all uplink channels except for PRACH since PRCH input is IQFP format without SDEC in use.

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Technology | Thor BB | Thor RU | UL channels & Signals |
| FR1-FDD-OBSAI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-TDD-CPRI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS, RIM-RS |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | - | supported | PUSCH/DMRS, SRS, COMMON-UL for RI detection, [CB012564-B] RIM-RS [End CB012564-B] |
| FR2-TDD-CPRI | - | - | - |
| FR2-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |

---

#### 2.5.2.4.3 fdAgcGain

**2.5.2.4.3.0-2**  (ID: `11419377`)

fdAgcGain
Thor PRCH gets only FD samples input, and performs frequency domain automatic gain control after coherent combination. This function can be enabled with FDAGC\_ON of PRCH\_JOB\_CFG\_S.

When FDAGC\_ON = 0, then fdAgcGain = 1;

When FDAGC\_ON = 1, the targeted signal power at the output of FD-AGC is controlled by software with a back-off value specified in FDAGC\_BACKOFF of PRCH\_JOB\_CFG\_S, such that

Target Signal Power = 3 dB x (31 - FDAGC\_BACKOFF);

In Thor, FDAGC is turned on and FDAGC\_BACKOFF is set to 12 per 5GMAX proposal.

Then PRCH calculates the average power within group and controls the gain of each group and each antenna independently and provide the fdAgcGain in the PRCH final report, so the final fdAgcGain shall be mean value of report gains of all groups and all antennas.

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Thor** | **UL channels & Signals** |
| FR1-FDD-OBSAI | supported | PRACH |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported | PRACH |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-CPRI | supported | PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | supported | PRACH |
| FR2-TDD-CPRI | - | - |
| FR2-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | PRACH |

In THOR, the conditions in which FDAGC is on or off are described in [11449625](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_fAFzA_vvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ).

---
