With PRACH channel specific processing of ZC sequence correlation and antenna coherent combine, two separate factors zcCorrScale and cohCombScale shall contribute the power scaling and they are calculated as below formulas:

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is:
zcCorrScale = 0.5 \* sqrt(L\_RA / N\_IFFT)[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.4.4-1)

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains the text "cohCombScale = cohCombLen". The text is in a light gray color against a white background.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.4.4-2)

The IFFT and non-coherent combing shall introduce below two scales

[image-2][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation reads: `idftScale = sqrt(N_IFFT)`. The text is in a light gray color against a white background. The font appears to be a sans-serif font. The equation is presented in a single line.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2]     (equation 2.5.2.4.4-3)

and

[image-3][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula. The formula is written as:
nonCohCombScale = $\sqrt{\frac{numSeqReps}{cohComLen}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3]    (equation 2.5.2.4.4-4)

where here [image-4][image\_desc]The image contains the text "N IFFT" in a blue font. The text is slightly blurry.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.005.png[/image\_path][/image-4] = 512 for PRACH short formats with preamble length LRA = 139 and NIFFT = 2048 for PRACH long formats with preamble length LRA = 839, here[image-5][image\_desc]The image contains the text "cohCombLen" in a light gray, italicized font. The text is positioned at the bottom of the image, against a white background.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.006.png[/image\_path][/image-5] is the actual coherent combing length, [image-6][image\_desc]The image contains the text "numSeqReps" in a light gray, italicized font. The text is blurry and appears to be on a white background.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.007.png[/image\_path][/image-6] is the number of sequence repetitions.

The final power profile from PRCH output is taking the power contribution from multiple RX antennas in, to keep consistent with 5GMAX, the contribution shall be considered as power scaling  to be rescaled via square root of number of ative antennas, also the power profile output is integer value, then the floating point input conversion is to be considered via

[image-7][image\_desc]convScale = 15[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.008.png[/image\_path][/image-7]

For CPRI case and

**[Before CNI-84178]**

[image-8][image\_desc]The image contains the text "convScale = 14" in a light gray color against a white background. The text is in a serif font.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.009.png[/image\_path][/image-8]

For eCPRI case

**[CNI-84178]**

[image-9][image\_desc]The image contains the text "convScale = 15" in a light gray color against a white background. The text is in a sans-serif font.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.010.png[/image\_path][/image-9]

For eCPRI case

**[End CNI-84178]**

So final prchScalingFactor shall be calculated as

[image-10][image\_desc]prchScalingFactor = convScale · zcCorrScale · idftScale · cohCombScale · nonCohCombScale / sqrt(numAntComb)[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.011.png[/image\_path][/image-10]    (equation 2.6.2.4.4-5)

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported | PRACH |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-CPRI | supported | PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | PRACH |

#### 2.5.2.4.6 nShift

11419485:
nShift
Frequency domain dynamic scaling is introduced here in Thor **for both CPRI and eCPRI case and the algorithm is very similar to Loki and applicable to all uplink channels except for PRACH since fdAgcGain is used for PRACH. The calculation of nShift can refer to section [11419208](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-cNOvvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) for detail.**

I/Q are samples of the OFDM symbols for the corresponding UL physical channels of a specific UE per antenna wise and I/Q format depends on definition of each traffic channel for both CPRI and eCPRI.

xTarget is a predefined target value. Current proposed value is 12 with 3 bits margin and may be further tuned by fixed point based performance evaluation.

Left shift when nShift is positive value, and right shift when nShift is negative value, so L1SW needs to rescale this in measurements computation via below equation

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains the mathematical expression "2^n.shift". The text is in a light blue color and is slightly blurry. The exponent "n.shift" is smaller than the base "2" and is positioned above and to the right of it.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3096.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.4.6-1)

More channel specific details are written in section [11421822](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-hFvPvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ).

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Thor BB** | **Thor RU** | **UL channels & Signals** |

| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-TDD-CPRI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS, RIM-RS |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | - | supported | PUSCH/DMRS, SRS, COMMON-UL for RI detection, **[CB012564-B] RIM-RS** [End CB012564-B]\*\*\*\* |

#### 2.5.2.4.7 staticLShift and staticRShift

**2.5.2.4.7.0-1**  (ID: `11419496`)

staticLShift and staticRShift
For PUCCH streams, a fixed scaling up is performed in Thor RU (Refer to [11422696](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-iT2PvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) and FH mode change from mode 2 (9 bit mantissa + 3 bit exponent) to mode 1 (9 bit mantissa + 4 bit exponent), while currently no scaling down shall be done in CE job to avoid saturation, then **[Before PR840573] staticLShift = 7 bits [PR840573] staticLShift = 9 bits [End PR840573] and**

staticRShift = 0 bits shall be taken into account into PUCCH scaler calculation in RX power scaling formulas defined in [11422159](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-hswfvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ).

This requirement shall be applied only to sub-cell types C8\_2, C8\_4 and C8\_8 in L1 BB.

| fdAgcGain | Not applicable | Not applicable | Calculated | Not applicable |

fftScalingFactor
ULFE in Odin uses unnormalized FFT form,  the power in frequency domain shall be scaled up to NFFT times of the one in time domain, then L1SW needs to rescale this down in measurements computation via fftScalingFactor, which is equivalent to Spost defined in 5GMAX specification. This fftScalingFactor is applicable to all uplink channels including PRACH, which uses ULFE to perform FFT after sample rate conversion since no FFT in PRCH in Odin (Reference: [13349511](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_TCcmo-rAEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), and PRACH FFT size can be different from the one used for traffic channel, it depends on PRACH format  and same as PRACH IFFT size, so to differentiate the two:

For traffic channel:

`fftScalingFactor = sqrt(N_FFT)`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3081.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.5.1-1)

where, [image-1][image\_desc]The image contains the text "NFFT" in a light blue, serif font. The text is positioned in the bottom left corner of the image.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3081.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1] depends on BW and sampling rate.

#### 2.5.2.5.2 comExp

**2.5.2.5.2.0-1**  (ID: `12580734`)

comExp
SDEC in Odin is used to decompress data in IQFP format and converts it into eFXP format per each PRB group, and each sample in eFXP format is composed of a 16-bit mantissa for I and Q and groups of samples share one exponent. Then 16-bit mantissa after SDEC is used in subsequent data path of traffic channel without shared exponent in data processing, so L1SW needs to rescale this in measurements computation via **2^(-comExp). This comExp is applicable to all uplink channels except for PRACH since PRCH input is IQFP format without SDEC in use.**

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Odin BB** | **Odin RU** | **UL channels & Signals** |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | **[CB012115-SR-JA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-JA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-LA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-LA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-IA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-IA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS, **[CB012115-SR-MD] COMMON UL for RI detection, RIM-RS**[End CB012115-SR-MD]\*\*\*\* |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-GA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-GA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUCCH/DMRS |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | - | **[CB012115-SR-HA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-HA]\*\*\*\* | PUSCH/DMRS, SRS, **[CB012115-SR-HD] COMMON UL for RI detection, RIM-RS**[End CB012115-SR-HD]\*\*\*\* |

---

#### 2.5.2.5.3 fdAgcGain

**2.5.2.5.3.0-1**  (ID: `12580914`)

fdAgcGain
Odin PRCH gets only FD samples input, and performs frequency domain automatic gain control after coherent combination. This function can be enabled with FDAGC\_ON of PRCH\_JOB\_CFG\_S.

When FDAGC\_ON = 0, then fdAgcGain = 1;

When FDAGC\_ON = 1, the targeted signal power at the output of FD-AGC is controlled by software with a back-off value specified in FDAGC\_BACKOFF of PRCH\_JOB\_CFG\_S, such that

Target Signal Power = 3 dB x (31 - FDAGC\_BACKOFF);

In Odin, FDAGC is turned on and FDAGC\_BACKOFF is set to 12 per 5GMAX proposal.

Then PRCH calculates the average power within group and controls the gain of each group and each antenna independently and provide the fdAgcGain in the PRCH final report, so the final fdAgcGain shall be mean value of report gains of all groups and all antennas.

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Odin BB** | **Odin RU** | **UL channels & Signals** |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | **[CB012115-SR-JA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-JA]\*\*\*\* | - | PRACH |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-LA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-LA]\*\*\*\* | - | PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-IA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-IA]\*\*\*\* | - | PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-GA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-GA]\*\*\*\* | - | PRACH |

---

With PRACH channel specific processing of ZC sequence correlation and antenna coherent combine, two separate factors zcCorrScale and cohCombScale shall contribute the power scaling and they are calculated as below formulas:

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is:
zcCorrScale = 0.5 \* sqrt(L\_RA / N\_IFFT)[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.5.4-1)

The text is in a light gray color against a white background.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.5.4-2)

The IFFT and non-coherent combing shall introduce below two scales

[image-2][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation reads: `idftScale = sqrt(N_IFFT)`. The text is in a light gray color against a white background. The font appears to be a sans-serif font. The equation is presented in a single line.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2]     (equation 2.5.2.5.4-3)

and

[image-3][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula. The formula is written as:
nonCohCombScale = $\sqrt{\frac{numSeqReps}{cohComLen}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3]    (equation 2.5.2.5.4-4)

where here [image-4][image\_desc]The image contains the text "N IFFT" in a blue font. The text is slightly blurry.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.005.png[/image\_path][/image-4] = 512 for PRACH short formats with preamble length LRA = 139 and NIFFT = 2048 for PRACH long formats with preamble length LRA = 839, here[image-5][image\_desc]The image contains the text "cohCombLen" in a light gray, italicized font. The text is positioned at the bottom of the image, against a white background.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.006.png[/image\_path][/image-5] is the actual coherent combing length, [image-6][image\_desc]The image contains the text "numSeqReps" in a light gray, italicized font. The text is blurry and appears to be on a white background.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.007.png[/image\_path][/image-6] is the number of sequence repetitions.

The final power profile from PRCH output is taking the power contribution from multiple RX antennas in, to keep consistent with 5GMAX, the contribution shall be considered as power scaling  to be rescaled via square root of number of active antennas, also the power profile output is integer value, then the floating point input conversion is to be considered via

[image-7][image\_desc]convScale = 15[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.008.png[/image\_path][/image-7]

So final prchScalingFactor shall be calculated as

[image-8][image\_desc]prchScalingFactor = convScale · zcCorrScale · idftScale · cohCombScale · nonCohCombScale / sqrt(numAntComb)[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3090.011.png[/image\_path][/image-8]    (equation 2.5.2.5.4-5)

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Odin BB** | **Odin RU** | **UL channels & Signals** |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | **[CB012115-SR-JA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-JA]\*\*\*\* | - | PRACH |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-LA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-LA]\*\*\*\* | - | PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-IA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-IA]\*\*\*\* | - | PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-GA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-GA]\*\*\*\* | - | PRACH |

The decimation chain is implemented to perform reduced size FFT, and decimateScalingFactor shall be calculated as

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula. The formula is for "decimateScalingFactor" and is expressed as:
decimateScalingFactor = $\frac{(DecimRatio0)^5 \cdot 2^{-(OutputLevelAtten0)}}{\sqrt{(DecimRatio0) \cdot (2^{(OversampleRatio0)})}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.5.5-1)

Where here OversampleRatio0, DecimRatio0 and OutputLevelAtten0 are parameters configured in ULFE\_NORMAL\_JOB\_S. Below paragraph explains how to calculate the parameters to be configured.

Assuming FFTLength is the parameter configured according to the cell’s sampling rate per different bandwidth, FFTSizeDec is the parameter configured per the request of PRCH handling (2048 for long format and 512 for short format), and FFTSize is the least common multiple of the FFTLength and FFTSizeDec, then

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a single line of text in a serif font. The text reads: "DecimRatio0 = FFTSize / FFTSizeDec".[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.5.5-2)

[image-2][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is: OversampleRatio0 = log₂(FFTSize / FFTLength). The text is in a light gray color and is italicized. The equation is centered horizontally in the image.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2]    (equation 2.5.2.5.5-3)

If [image-3][image\_desc]The image contains the text "DecimRatio0" in a light gray, italicized font. The text is positioned at the bottom of the image against a white background.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3] is larger than 1 (the range of [image-4][image\_desc]The image contains the text "DecimRatio0" in a light gray color against a white background. The text is in a serif font and appears to be slightly italicized.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.005.png[/image\_path][/image-4]is from 2 to 48), then

[image-5][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray font on a white background. The formula is:
OutputLevelAtten0 = round (26 - (log₂(48 / DecimRatio0))) \* 5)
The formula appears to be a definition or calculation for a variable named "OutputLevelAtten0". It involves rounding a calculation that includes a logarithm base 2, a division, and a multiplication.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.006.png[/image\_path][/image-5]    (equation 2.5.2.5.5-4)

Else

[image-6][image\_desc]The image contains the text "OutputLevelAtten0 = 0". The text is in a light gray color against a white background. The font appears to be a serif font.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3070.007.png[/image\_path][/image-6]    (equation 2.5.2.5.5-5)

#### 2.5.2.5.6 nShift

**2.5.2.5.6.0-1**  (ID: `12580744`)

nShift
12580744:
nShift
12580744:

12580744:
nShift
Frequency domain dynamic scaling is introduced here in Odin and applicable to all uplink channels except for PRACH since fdAgcGain is used for PRACH.

The algorithm is to calculate shift factor “nShift” equal to delta between target and MSB as below[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray font on a white background. The formula is:
`nShift = xTarget - length(dec2bin(2^Q_IQ-in * max(|I|, |Q|))) antenna wise, one OFDM symbol`
The formula appears to be related to signal processing, possibly in the context of wireless communications or digital signal processing. Specifically, it defines a variable `nShift` in terms of `xTarget`, the length of a binary representation of a calculated value, and some parameters like `Q_IQ-in`, `I`, and `Q`. The terms "antenna wise" and "OFDM symbol" suggest its application in a multi-antenna Orthogonal Frequency-Division Multiplexing system.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3073.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.5.6-1)

where,

I/Q are samples of the OFDM symbols for the corresponding UL physical channels of a specific UE per antenna wise and I/Q Q format depends on definition of each traffic channel.

xTarget is a predefined target value. Current proposed value is 12 with 3 bits margin.

Left shift when nShift is positive value, and right shift when nShift is negative value, so L1SW needs to rescale this in measurements computation via below equation

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains the mathematical expression "2^n.shift". The text is in a light blue color and is slightly blurry. The exponent "n.shift" is smaller than the base "2" and is positioned above and to the right of it.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3096.001.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.5.6-2)

More channel specific details are written in section [12582289](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_EqypsDRXEfCKaNlcHOQWmg).

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Odin BB** | **Odin RU** | **UL channels & Signals** |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | **[CB012115-SR-JA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-JA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-LA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-LA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-IA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-IA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS,  **[CB012115-SR-MD] COMMON UL for RI detection, RIM-RS**[End CB012115-SR-MD]\*\*\*\* |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-GA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-GA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUCCH/DMRS |

#### 2.5.2.5.7 staticLShift and staticRShift

**2.5.2.5.7.0-1**  (ID: `12631768`)

staticLShift and staticRShift
For PUCCH streams, a fixed scaling up is performed in Odin RU (Refer to [12631771: staticLShift and staticRShift](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_Y40aRjxPEfCYiuaHdt7wgQ)) and FH mode change from mode 2 (9 bit mantissa + 3 bit exponent) to mode 1 (9 bit mantissa + 4 bit exponent), while currently no scaling down shall be done in CE job to avoid saturation, then staticLShift = 9 bits and

staticRShift = 0 bits shall be taken into account into PUCCH scaler calculation in RX power scaling formulas defined in [12582292: Rx power scaling formulas for PUCCH](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_W5mjgDRXEfCKaNlcHOQWmg).

This requirement shall be applied only to sub-cell types C8\_2, C8\_4 and C8\_8 in L1 BB.

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Odin BB** | **Odin RU** | **UL channels & Signals** |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-HE] supported** [End CB012115-SR-HE]\*\*\*\* | - | PUCCH/DMRS |

### 2.5.2.6 Parameters for L1 Radio Specific

#### 2.5.2.6.1 For Thor only

##### 2.5.2.6.1.1 powerScaingFactor

###### 2.5.2.6.1.1.1 For Channel or signal excluding RAW SRS

**2.5.2.6.1.1.1.0-5**  (ID: `13347875`)

For Channel or signal excluding RAW SRS
**For Thor eCPRI 7-2e case:**

L1 (radio) shall calculate powerScalingFactor for PUSCH, aSRS, pSRS for SU-MIMO, COMMON-UL for RI detection, and RIM-RS according to below formula:

*powerScalingFactor = referenceLevel - (gainCorrection - bfGain) (dBm)*

Where referenceLevel is -152 dBm hardcoded in L1 (radio), gainCorrection is received from OAM (See Note1) configured for eCPRI 7-2a PUCCH, here used in powerScalingFactor calculation for PUSCH, aSRS, pSRS for SU-MIMO, COMMON-UL for RI detection,**and RIM-RS, and bfGain should be calculated by L1 (radio) according to below equation:**

*bfGain = -10log10(numRxAntennas)**(dB)*\*\*

Where numRxAntennas represents number of RX antenna array elements used to receive the channel on one polarization with **assumption that the amplitude of beamforming weight on each element is 1.**

Since the 5G beamforming weights are non-normalized, RU Thor shall need to remove the beamforming gain during digital beamforming operation, and for efficient HW or SW handling, RF7.1 UL level plan split this beamforming gain compensation to two parts. (Reference: [13349540](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_Lvi5YOrDEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw) §1.9.4.3 L1low beamforming configuration in THOR)

Part1 Done in Mars (As Mars can't differentiate channel or signal, the compensation is applied to all uplink channels or signals):

*MarsGain =*bfGain - gainOfBeamModule\*\*

Part2 Done in Thor (For those channels or signals which need to perform digital beamforming):

**gainOfBeamModule = -10*log10(power(2, 2*UL\_RshiftBits)) (dB)**

**UL\_RshiftBits = ceil(10*log10(NantRX)/(20*log10(2)))**

where NantRX is number of RX antenna per polarity, e.g. 32 for AVQL and 16 for AVQC, so

1) For 64TRX radios, bfGain = -15 dB and gainOfBeamModule = -18 dB, a 3dB gap present.

2) For 32TRX radios, bfGain = -12 dB and gainOfBeamModule = -12 dB, no gap present.

For PUSCH/aSRS/COMMON-UL for RI detection/RIM-RS, Part2 compensation is achieved by exponent shift with UL\_RshiftBits in ARXE mode 4.

For pSRS for SU-MIMO, Part2 compensation is achieved by applying  UL\_RshiftBits during digital beamforming in DSP.

**Note:**

**[Before CB014308-B]**

1. For the definition of gainCorrection, see §3.6.9 LowLevelRxLink in M-plane IDT (Reference: [13349502](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_vOm1A-qtEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw))

[**CB014308-B]**

1. For the definition of gainCorrection, MOs for PUCCH transferring are reused:

1.1> When M-Plane protocol is RP1/SOAP (Reference: [13349502](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_vOm1A-qtEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), L1 UL PHY shall refer to §3.6.9 LowLevelRxLink in M-plane IDT.

1.2> When M-Plane protocol is NCY (Reference: [13349503](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_MugokOquEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), L1 UL PHY shall refer to eaxc-gain-correction in low-level-rx-endpoints (see [11431489](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_uCD3AfvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) and [11431505](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_uG56wPvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) and gain-correction in rx-array-carriers (see [11431939](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_wFgVcfvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) and [11431947](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_wIILqvvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) and sum of the both (see [11414438](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_E8QMwPvmEe-AqvopbP1qhQ))

[End **CB014308-B]**

1. For the calculation of gainCorrection, please refer to [11689735](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_oB6bMPwjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) (bfGain included).
2. Power scaling of PUCCH and PRACH shall follow legacy eCPRI 7-2a rule defined in [11418797](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-aYD_vvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ).
3. PTRS is not supported in eCPRI 7-2e.
4. New term ru\_gain\_correct\_scs\_channel is included into gainCorrection inside BOAM for cMMAr7.1 radios,the value definition of ru\_gain\_correct\_scs\_channel for each channel in Reference [13349505](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_E6UeFOqvEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw).
5. The gainCorrection value from MOs for PUCCH transferring (see note1) is still used for powerScalingFactor calculation for above mentioned channels or signals. Then CB014612-SR-A doesn't contain functional change.

---

###### 2.5.2.6.1.1.2 For RAW SRS only

**2.5.2.6.1.1.2.0-4**  (ID: `13347874`)

For RAW SRS only
**For Thor eCPRI 7-2e case:**

L1 (radio) shall calculate powerScalingFactorSrs for **RAW SRS according to below formula:**

*powerScalingFactorSrs = referenceLevel - (gainCorrection - gainOfBeamModule) (dBm)*

Where referenceLevel is -152 dBm hardcoded in L1 (radio), gainCorrection is received from OAM (See Note1) configured for eCPRI 7-2a PUCCH, here used in powerScalingFactorSrs calculation for RAW SRS, and gainOfBeamModule (See Note2) shall be calculated by L1 (radio) according to below equation

**gainOfBeamModule = -10*log10(power(2, 2*UL\_RshiftBits)) (dB)**

**UL\_RshiftBits = ceil(10*log10(NantRX)/(20*log10(2)))**

where NantRX is number of RX antenna per polarity, e.g. 32 for AVQL and 16 for AVQC, so

1) For 64TRX radios, bfGain = -15 dB and gainOfBeamModule = -18 dB, a 3dB gap present.

2) For 32TRX radios, bfGain = -12 dB and gainOfBeamModule = -12 dB, no gap present.

Since the 5G beamforming weights are non-normalized, RU Thor shall need to remove the beamforming gain during digital beamforming operation, and for efficient HW or SW handling, RF7.1 UL level plan split this beamforming gain compensation to two parts. (Reference: [13349540](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_Lvi5YOrDEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw) §1.9.4.3 L1low beamforming configuration in THOR)

Part1 Done in Mars (As Mars can't differentiate channel or signal, the compensation is applied to all uplink channels or signals):

**bfGain - gainOfBeamModule**

Part2 Done in Thor (For those channels or signals which need to perform digital beamforming):

**gainOfBeamModule = -10*log10(power(2, 2*UL\_RshiftBits)) (dB)**

**UL\_RshiftBits = ceil(10*log10(NantRX)/(20*log10(2)))**

where NantRX is number of RX antenna per polarity, e.g. 32 for AVQL**.**

When power is calculated based on RAW SRS data per antenna and no digital beamforming is performed, so part2 compensation in Thor is not needed, while part1 compensation in Mars still exists, then L1 (Radio) need to use above powerScaingFactorSRS other than the one defined powerScalingFactor in [11422618](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-hszfvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) for final power measurement report.

Above requirement shall be applicable to SRS port power measurement for real time beamforming.

**Note:**

**[Before CB014308-B]**

1. For the definition of gainCorrection, see §3.6.9 LowLevelRxLink in M-plane IDT (Reference: [13349502](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_vOm1A-qtEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)).

[**CB014308-B]**

1. For the definition of gainCorrection, MOs for PUCCH transferring are reused:

1.1> When M-Plane protocol is RP1/SOAP (Reference: [13349502](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_vOm1A-qtEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), L1 UL PHY shall refer to §3.6.9 LowLevelRxLink in M-plane IDT.

1.2> When M-Plane protocol is NCY (Reference: [13349503](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_MugokOquEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), L1 UL PHY shall refer to eaxc-gain-correction in low-level-rx-endpoints (see [11431489](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_uCD3AfvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)  and [11431505](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_uG56wPvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) and gain-correction in rx-array-carriers (see [11431939](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_wFgVcfvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) and sum of the both (see [11414438](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_E8QMwPvmEe-AqvopbP1qhQ))

[End **CB014308-B]**

1. For the calculation of gainCorrection, please refer to [11689735](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_oB6bMPwjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) (bfGain included).
2. For the definition of gainOfBeamModule, see Reference: [13349540](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_Lvi5YOrDEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw) §1.9.4.3 L1low beamforming configuration in THOR.
3. New term ru\_gain\_correct\_scs\_channel is included into gainCorrection inside BOAM for cMMAr7.1 radios, the value definition of ru\_gain\_correct\_scs\_channel for each channel in Reference [13349505](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_E6UeFOqvEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw).  15dB (compared with 12dB for other channels) is defined for SRS for 64TRX radios, which is mainly for additional 3dB compensation for L1Hi in 7-2a FH.
4. The gainCorrection value from MOs for PUCCH transferring (see note1) is still used for powerScalingFactor calculation for RAW SRS Since one scaling is used in Mars for non-PRACH stream, and the 3dB compensation is already implemented with above formula for powerScalingFactorSrs calculation. Then CB014612-SR-A doesn't contain functional change.

Frequency domain dynamic scaling is introduced here. The algorithm is to calculate shift factor “nShift” equal to delta between target and MSB as below

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray color against a white background. The formula is:
`nShift = xTarget - length(dec2bin(2^IQ-in * max(|I|, |Q|) antenna wise, one OFDM symbol))`
The text is in a serif font, and some characters are superscripts or subscripts. [image-1][image\_desc]The image contains the text "2n.shift" in a blue font. The text is slightly blurry.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3217.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.6.1.2-2)

##### 2.5.2.6.1.3 staticLShift and staticRshift

**2.5.2.6.1.3.0-1**  (ID: `11422703`)

staticLShift and staticRshift
In eCPRI 7-2e, in order to decrease DSP load, PUSCH SW complexity and HW resource requirement, full dynamic scaling shall be replaced by fixed left shift in ARXE M4 (BF job), optional fixed right shift in CE job and optional dynamic scaling in CE job which is channel or signal dependent.

1. Use common BF job for PUSCH, PUCCH, aSRS, RIM-RSSI and RIM-RS with fixed scaling up, then **[Before PR840573] staticLShift = 7 (bits)** [PR840573] staticLShift = 9 (bits) **[End PR840573].**\*\*\*\*
2. For PUSCH, fixed scaling down within CE job, then staticRShift = 2 (bits).
3. For PUCCH, currently no scaling down in CE job but dynamic scaling in Thor BB. (Refer to [11419491](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-dbV_vvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) staticLShift and staticRShift and [11419451](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-dbUvvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) nShift.)
4. For aSRS, currently no scaling down in CE job, then staticRShift = 0 (bits) and dynamic scaling in Thor RU. (Refer to [11422674](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-iT1vvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) nShift.)
5. For RIM-RS, currently no scaling down in CE job, then staticRShift = 0 (bits) and dynamic scaling in Thor RU. (Refer to [11422674](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-iT1vvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) nShift.)

**[Before PR840573]**

**[Before PR826436]**

1. For RIM-RSSI, currently no scaling down in CE job, then staticRShift = 0 (bits) and dynamic scaling in Thor RU. (Refer to [11422674](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-iT1vvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) nShift.)

**[PR826436]**

1. For RIM-RSSI, currently no scaling down in CE job, then staticRShift = 7 (bits) and no dynamic scaling in Thor RU. (Refer to [11422674](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-iT1vvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) nShift.)

**[End PR826436]**

**[PR840573]**

1. For RIM-RSSI, currently no scaling down in CE job, then staticRShift = 9 (bits) and no dynamic scaling in Thor RU. (Refer to [11422674](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-iT1vvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) nShift.)

**[End PR840573]**

#### 2.5.2.6.2 For Odin only

##### 2.5.2.6.2.1 powerScalingFactor

###### 2.5.2.6.2.1.1 For Channel or signal excluding RAW SRS

**2.5.2.6.2.1.1.0-1**  (ID: `12582507`)

For Channel or signal excluding RAW SRS
**For Odin eCPRI 7-2e case:**

L1 (radio) shall calculate powerScalingFactor for PUSCH, aSRS, pSRS for SU-MIMO, [**CB012115-SR-HD] COMMON-UL for RI detection and RIM-RS [End**CB012115-SR-HD] according to below formula:\*\*\*\*

*powerScalingFactor = referenceLevel - (gainCorrection - bfGain) (dBm)*

Where referenceLevel is -152 dBm hardcoded in L1 (radio), gainCorrection is received from OAM (See Note1) configured for eCPRI 7-2a PUCCH, here used in powerScalingFactor calculation for PUSCH, aSRS, pSRS for SU-MIMO, COMMON-UL for RI detection, **and RIM-RS, and bfGain should be calculated by L1 (radio) according to below equation:**

*bfGain = -10log10(numRxAntennas)**(dB)*\*\*

Where numRxAntennas represents number of RX antenna array elements used to receive the channel on one polarization with **assumption that the amplitude of beamforming weight on each element is 1.**

Since the 5G beamforming weights are non-normalized, RU Odin shall need to remove the beamforming gain during digital beamforming operation, and for efficient HW or SW handling, two parts are implemented

Part1 Done in Mercury (As Mercury can't differentiate channel or signal, the compensation is applied to all uplink channels or signals):

**bfGain - gainOfBeamModule**

Part2 Done in Odin (For those channels or signals which need to perform digital beamforming):

**gainOfBeamModule = -10*log10(power(2, 2*UL\_RshiftBits)) (dB)**

**UL\_RshiftBits = ceil(10*log10(NantRX)/(20*log10(2)))**

where NantRX is number of RX antenna per polarity**.**

For PUSCH/aSRS/[**CB012115-SR-HD]COMMON-UL for RI detection/RIM-RS[End**CB012115-SR-HD], Part2 compensation is achieved by exponent shift with UL\_RshiftBits in ARXE mode 4.\*\*\*\*

For pSRS for SU-MIMO, Part2 compensation is achieved by applying  UL\_RshiftBits during digital beamforming in DSP.

**Note:**

**[Before CB012115-SR-HQ]**

1. For the definition of gainCorrection, see §3.6.9 LowLevelRxLink in M-plane IDT (Reference: [13349502](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_vOm1A-qtEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)) and for the calculation of gainCorrection, please refer to [11689735](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_oB6bMPwjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) (bfGain included).
2. Power scaling of PUCCH and PRACH shall follow legacy eCPRI 7-2a rule defined in [11418797](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-aYD_vvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ).
3. PTRS is not supported in eCPRI 7-2e.

[**CB012115-SR-HQ]**

1. For the definition of gainCorrection, MOs for PUCCH transferring are reused:

1.1> When M-Plane protocol is RP1/SOAP (Reference: [13349502](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_vOm1A-qtEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), L1 UL PHY shall refer to §3.6.9 LowLevelRxLink in M-plane IDT.

1.2> When M-Plane protocol is NCY (Reference: [13349503](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_MugokOquEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), L1 UL PHY shall refer to eaxc-gain-correction in low-level-rx-endpoints (see [11431489](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_uCD3AfvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)  and [11431505](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_uG56wPvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) and gain-correction in rx-array-carriers (see [11431939](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_wFgVcfvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) and sum of the both (see [11414438](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_E8QMwPvmEe-AqvopbP1qhQ))

1. RF9 Odin shall only support M-Plane protocol NCY. L1 Radio is developed based on RP1/SOAP at early phase. Once implementation on NCY is ready, supporting on RP1/SOAP will be stopped.
2. For the calculation of gainCorrection and eaxc-gain-correction, please refer to [11689735](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_oB6bMPwjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) (bfGain included).
3. Power scaling of PUCCH and PRACH shall follow legacy eCPRI 7-2a rule defined in [11418797](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-aYD_vvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ).
4. PTRS is not supported in eCPRI 7-2e.

[End **CB012115-SR-HQ]**

---

###### 2.5.2.6.2.1.2 For RAW SRS only

**2.5.2.6.2.1.2.0-1**  (ID: `12582512`)

For RAW SRS only
**For Odin eCPRI 7-2e case:**

L1 (radio) shall calculate powerScalingFactorSrs for **RAW SRS according to below formula:**

*powerScalingFactorSrs = referenceLevel - (gainCorrection - gainOfBeamModule) (dBm)*

Where referenceLevel is -152 dBm hardcoded in L1 (radio), gainCorrection is received from OAM (See Note1) configured for eCPRI 7-2a PUCCH, here used in powerScalingFactorSrs calculation for RAW SRS, and gainOfBeamModule (See Note2) shall be calculated by L1 (radio) according to below equation

**gainOfBeamModule = -10*log10(power(2, 2*UL\_RshiftBits)) (dB)**

**UL\_RshiftBits = ceil(10*log10(NantRX)/(20*log10(2)))**

where NantRX is number of RX antenna per polarity**.**

Since the 5G beamforming weights are non-normalized, RU Odin shall need to remove the beamforming gain during digital beamforming operation, and for efficient HW or SW handling, two parts are implemented:

Part1 Done in Mercury (As Mercury can't differentiate channel or signal, the compensation is applied to all uplink channels or signals):

**bfGain - gainOfBeamModule**

Part2 Done in Odin (For those channels or signals which need to perform digital beamforming):

**gainOfBeamModule = -10*log10(power(2, 2*UL\_RshiftBits)) (dB)**

**UL\_RshiftBits = ceil(10*log10(NantRX)/(20*log10(2)))**

where NantRX is number of RX antenna per polarity**.**

When power is calculated based on RAW SRS data per antenna and no digital beamforming is performed, so part2 compensation in Thor is not needed, while part1 compensation in Mercury still exists, then L1 (Radio) need to use above powerScaingFactorSRS other than the one defined powerScalingFactor in [11422618](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-hszfvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) for final power measurement report.

Above requirement shall be applicable to SRS port power measurement for real time beamforming.

**Note:**

**[Before CB012115-SR-HQ]**

1. For the definition of gainCorrection, see §3.6.9 LowLevelRxLink in M-plane IDT (Reference: [13349502](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_vOm1A-qtEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)) and for the calculation of gainCorrection, please refer to [11689735](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_oB6bMPwjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) (bfGain included).

[**CB012115-SR-HQ]**

1. For the definition of gainCorrection, MOs for PUCCH transferring are reused:

1.1> When M-Plane protocol is RP1/SOAP (Reference: [13349502](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_vOm1A-qtEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), L1 UL PHY shall refer to §3.6.9 LowLevelRxLink in M-plane IDT.

1.2> When M-Plane protocol is NCY (Reference: [13349503](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_MugokOquEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw)), L1 UL PHY shall refer to eaxc-gain-correction in low-level-rx-endpoints (see [11431489](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_uCD3AfvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)  and [11431505](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_uG56wPvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) and gain-correction in rx-array-carriers (see [11431939](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_wFgVcfvnEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)) and sum of the both (see [11414438](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_E8QMwPvmEe-AqvopbP1qhQ))

1. RF9 Odin shall only support M-Plane protocol NCY. L1 Radio is developed based on RP1/SOAP at early phase. Once implementation on NCY is ready, supporting on RP1/SOAP will be stopped.
2. For the calculation of gainCorrection and eaxc-gain-correction, please refer to [11689735](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_oB6bMPwjEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) (bfGain included).

[End **CB012115-SR-HQ]**

##### 2.5.2.6.2.2 nShift

**2.5.2.6.2.2.0-1**  (ID: `12632621`)

nShift
12632621:
nShift
12632621:
nShift
12632621:
nShift
12632621:
nShift
12632621:
nShift
12632621:
nShift
12632621:
nShift
12632621:
nShift
12632621:
nShift
12632621:
nShift
Frequency domain dynamic scaling is introduced here. The algorithm is to calculate shift factor “nShift” equal to delta between target and MSB as below

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray color against a white background. The formula is:
`nShift = xTarget - length(dec2bin(2^IQ-in * max(|I|, |Q|) antenna wise, one OFDM symbol))`
The text is in a serif font, and some characters are superscripts or subscripts. The formula appears to be related to signal processing or digital communications, possibly concerning the calculation of a shift value in an OFDM (Orthogonal Frequency-Division Multiplexing) system.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3217.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.2.6.2.2-1)

Where,

I/Q are samples of the OFDM symbols for the corresponding UL physical channels of a specific UE per antenna wise and I/Q format depends on definition of each traffic channel for eCPRI.

xTarget is a predefined target value. Current proposed value is 13 with 3 bits margin and may be further tuned by fixed point based performance evaluation.

Left shift when nShift is positive value, and right shift when nShift is negative value, so L1SW needs to rescale this in measurements computation via below equation

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains the text "2n.shift" in a blue font. The text is slightly blurry.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3217.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.2.6.2.2-2)

[**CB012115-SR-HE]**

This dynamic scaling shall be only applied to aSRS, [**CB012115-SR-HD] RIM-RSSI and RIM-RS [End**CB012115-SR-HD] in Odin RU.\*\*\*\*

Note: PUCCH dynamic scaling is kept as legacy in Odin BB.

[End **CB012115-SR-HE]**

More channel specific details are written in section [12584291](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_pJPKYDUgEfCKaNlcHOQWmg).

##### 2.5.2.6.2.3 staticLShift and staticRShift

**2.5.2.6.2.3.0-1**  (ID: `12631779`)

staticLShift and staticRShift
In eCPRI 7-2e, in order to decrease DSP load, PUSCH SW complexity and HW resource requirement, full dynamic scaling shall be replaced by fixed left shift in ARXE M4 (BF job), optional fixed right shift in CE job and optional dynamic scaling in CE job which is channel or signal dependent.

1. Use common BF job for PUSCH, PUCCH, aSRS, [CB012115-SR-HD] RIM-RSSI and RIM-RS [End CB012115-SR-HD] with fixed scaling up, then**staticLShift = 9 (bits).**

3. For PUCCH, currently no scaling down in CE job but dynamic scaling in Odin BB. (Refer to [12580717: staticLShift and staticRShift](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_-S4uoDH0EfCfjdcwDn2YOQ)  and [12580714: nShift](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_0rVlkTH0EfCfjdcwDn2YOQ).)

[End CB012115-SR-HD]

## 2.5.3 Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas

**2.5.3.0-1**  (ID: `11419522`)

Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
11419522:
Conventions used to represent numbers in Rx power scaling formulas
Suppose a parameter called *parameter, with an internal binary representation in Q (1.x.y) format, appears in a formula (for example, a formula expressing an operation that needs to be performed by L1-SW on the parameter before it can be transferred to 5G-L2-PS).* parameter in the formula could mean the integer value corresponding to a binary integer represented in two’s complement with a sign bit (MSB) and x+y additional bits, in which case the real value represented in Q (1.x.y) format would be:\*\*

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains the text "parameter · 2⁻ʸ". The text is in a light blue color against a white background. The word "parameter" is written in italics. The dot between "parameter" and "2⁻ʸ" is a multiplication symbol. The exponent "⁻ʸ" is written in a smaller font size and is raised above the number 2.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3102.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.3-1)

The advantage of this convention is that the formula indicates how many bits there are in the Q format after the binary point, in other words the essential information on the used Q format is conveyed by the formula itself. The drawback is that, whenever the Q format of *parameter is changed, the formula describing the operation that needs to be performed by L1-SW on* parameter needs to be changed.\*\*

For that reason, in this document, a different convention is used. Whenever *parameter is used in a formula, it stands for the real value of* parameter represented in the Q (1.x.y) format, not for the integer value. The drawback is that the information on the Q format is lost, but the advantage is that the formula needs no longer be changed when the Q format is changed.\*\*

These different conventions explain why formulas in this specification and other specifications may look different.

---

## 2.5.4 Power unit used in the Rx digital processing chain

#### 2.5.4.1.1 Common rule

**2.5.4.1.1.0-1**  (ID: `11419563`)

Common rule
11419563:

Common rule
The power in mW corresponding to 1 LSB at the CPRI input is: [image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is "10 raised to the power of (0.1 \* rxScalingFactor) / 10". The base is 10, and the exponent is a fraction. The numerator of the fraction is "0.1 rxScalingFactor", and the denominator is "10".[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3106.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]

The binary format at the CPRI input is Q (1.0.14), very nearly representing real numbers between -1 and 1 (integers between -214 and 214).

The power in mW corresponding to amplitude 1 at the CPRI input is therefore [image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is approximately equal to the quantity $(2^{14} \cdot 10^{\frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20}})^2$.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3106.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]

This is the power unit in the whole digital Rx chain: whatever changes of Q format may happen in the Rx chain, real value 1 always corresponds to this power unit, unless scaling operations are performed on the signal.

If the signal is multiplied by “scaler”, then power (scaler)2 corresponds to a power in mW equal to [image-2][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression enclosed in parentheses and raised to the power of 2. The expression is:
$(2^{14} \cdot 10^{\frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20}})^2$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3106.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2], which means that the new power unit is, in mW, [image-3][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is a fraction. The numerator is enclosed in parentheses and raised to the power of 2. Inside the parentheses, there is a term $2^{14} \cdot 10$ multiplied by a fraction. The fraction in the numerator has $0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor$ in the numerator and $20$ in the denominator. The denominator of the main fraction is $scaler^2$.
The expression can be written as:
$$ \left( 2^{14} \cdot 10 \cdot \frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20} \right)^2 / scaler^2 $$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3106.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3]. In other words, any real number A representing power in this Rx chain can be converted to mW by performing the operation: [image-4][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is:
$A \cdot \left( \frac{2^{14} \cdot 10 \cdot \frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20}}{scaler^2} \right)^2$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3106.005.png[/image\_path][/image-4].

For Loki only
Below figure explains how the 15 bits are converted to 16 bits in CPRI receiver (CRX) block (Reference: [13349498](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/TX_8xSBwOqrEfCnwLcpJWh_Zw) § 4.7.4). If configuration register of CRX\_ULAW\_GENERAL:ALIGNMENT is set to 0, the 15 bits are mapped to the **most significant bits of the sample in the RP3 message. If configuration register bit CRX\_ULAW\_GENERAL:ALIGNMENT is set to 1, then 7-bit and 15-bit samples are mapped to the** least significant bits of the sample in the RP3 message (sign bit is extended to msb).\*\*\*\*

[image-0][image\_desc]The image displays two sections, each labeled with "ALIGNMENT = 0" and "ALIGNMENT = 1" respectively. Both sections contain rows of numbers and colored blocks, along with the text "rxScalingFactor" at the top right of each section.
**Section 1: ALIGNMENT = 0**
This section has two rows of data.
\* The first row shows numbers from 15 down to 0, with a single green block labeled "S" positioned above the number 15.
\* The second row also shows numbers from 15 down to 0. It has a green block labeled "S" above the number 15, and a blue block labeled "0" above the number 0.
**Section 2: ALIGNMENT = 1**
This section also has two rows of data.
\* The first row shows numbers from 15 down to 0, with a single green block labeled "S" positioned above the number 15.
\* The second row shows numbers from 15 down to 0. It has two green blocks, each labeled "S", positioned above the numbers 15 and 14 respectively.
The colored blocks appear to represent some form of data or status associated with the corresponding numbers. The green blocks labeled "S" seem to indicate a starting point or a specific value, while the blue block labeled "0" in the first section might represent a final value or a different state. The arrangement of the "S" blocks changes between the two alignment settings, suggesting that the alignment parameter influences how these blocks are positioned or repeated.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3109.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]

In case of ALIGNMENT equal to 0, the data is converted to Q (1.0.15) with 1 bit left shift, 2 times scale on integer value with 1 LSB mapped to rxScalingFactor; In case of ALIGNMENT equal to 1, the data is sign extended and is still equivalent to Q (1.0.14) and no scale on integer value with 1 LSB mapped to rxScalingFactor.

So no matter which configuration, the **bit width 14 (in case of ALIGNMENT = 0, 14 = (15-1) is used though Q format of input data is 1.0.15) with 1 LSB mapping to rxScalingFactor is always taken into power conversion. Currently ALIGNMENT is equal to 0 by default.**

**Note: the register ALIGNMENT is CPRI Link specific.**

Above requirement support based on technology and HW board as below table:

|  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **ABIO** | **ABIN** | **ASOE** | **ASOF** | **RINLINE1** |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported | supported | supported | **[CB009223-C] supported** [End CB009223-C]\*\*\*\* | supported |
| FR1-TDD-CPRI | supported | - | supported | **[CB009223-D] supported** [End CB009223-D]\*\*\*\* | supported |
| FR2-TDD-CPRI | - | - | - | - | - |

RINLINE 1 support is terminated in 24R1, requirement is not valid for RINLINE 1 starting from 24R2.

##### 2.5.4.2.1.0-1 For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only 11419629: For Loner only The reasoning for the eCPRI case is the same as for CPRI, the only difference being that the binary format at the output of the frequency domain IQ decompression stage is Q (1.10.14), instead of Q(1.0.14) at CPRI input. The reasoning for the eCPRI case is the same as for CPRI, the only difference being that the binary format at the output of the frequency domain IQ decompression stage is **Q (1.0.15) instead of Q (1.0.14) at CPRI input. Below figure explains how the 16 bits Q (1.0.15) are extracted from ORAN interface 24 bits Q (1.0.23) during eCPRI decompression. In case of EDEC HW in use, the power in dBm corresponding to 1 LSB of extracted 16 bits is always represented by rxScalingFactor. Hence any real number A representing power in the Rx chain is converted to mW in the eCPRI case by performing the operation:**

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is:
$A \left( \frac{2^{15} 10^{\frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20}}}{scaler^2} \right)^2$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3117.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]

|  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | - | - | supported |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | supported | supported | **[CB009223-B] supported** [End CB009223-B]\*\*\*\* | supported |
| FR2-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | - | - | - |

RINLINE 1 support is terminated in 24R1, requirement is not valid for RINLINE 1 starting from 24R2.

The reasoning for the eCPRI case is the same as for CPRI, the only difference being that the binary format at the output of SDEC with symbol decompression is **Q (1.0.15) regarding signed 16-bit mantissa. With IQFP (14-bit mantissa plus 4 bit exponent) used in EDEC and eFXP (16-bit mantissa plus 4 bit exponent) used in SDEC, Thor can handle at most 29-bit width dynamic range defined in ORAN interface, Here only 16-bit mantissa is used for subsequent data processing and 4 bit shared exponent value as scaling factor for final power measurement calculation. Hence any real number A prepreenting power in the Rx chain is converted to mW in the eCPRI case by performing the operation:**

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is:
$A \cdot \left( \frac{2^{15} \cdot 10^{\frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20}}}{scaler^2} \right)^2$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3122.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0].

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Thor** | **UL channels & Signals** |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS, PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS, PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | - | - |
| FR2-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | PUSCH/DMRS/PTRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS, PRACH |

#### 2.5.4.2.4 For Odin only

**2.5.4.2.4.0-1**  (ID: `12580826`)

For Odin only
12580826:
For Odin only

12580826:
For Odin only
12580826:
For Odin only
12580826:
For Odin only
The reasoning for the eCPRI case is the same as for CPRI, the only difference being that the binary format at the output of SDEC with symbol decompression is **Q (1.0.15) regarding signed 16-bit mantissa. With IQFP (14-bit mantissa plus 4 bit exponent) used in EDEC and eFXP (16-bit mantissa plus 4 bit exponent) used in SDEC, Odin can handle at most 29-bit width dynamic range defined in ORAN interface, Here only 16-bit mantissa is used for subsequent data processing and 4 bit shared exponent value as scaling factor for final power measurement calculation.**

Hence any real number A presenting power in the Rx chain is converted to mW in the eCPRI case by performing the operation:

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is:
$A \cdot \left( \frac{2^{15} \cdot 10^{\frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20}}}{scaler^2} \right)^2$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3122.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0].

The supported channel and signal based on technology as below table:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **Odin BB** | **Odin RU** | **UL channels & Signals** |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-LA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-LA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS, PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-IA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-IA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUSCH/DMRS, PUCCH/DMRS, SRS, PRACH, **[CB012115-SR-MD] COMMON UL for RI detection, RIM-RS**[End CB012115-SR-MD]\*\*\*\* |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | **[CB012115-SR-GA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-GA]\*\*\*\* | - | PUCCH/DMRS, PRACH |
| FR1-TDD-7-2e-eCPRI | - | **[CB012115-SR-HA] supported** [End CB012115-SR-HA]\*\*\*\* | PUSCH/DMRS, SRS, **[CB012115-SR-HD] COMMON UL for RI detection, RIM-RS**[End CB012115-SR-HD]\*\*\*\* |

---

### 2.5.4.4 Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases

#### 2.5.4.4.0-1 Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases For Loner only (ID: 11419743)

**2.5.4.4.0-1.0-1**  (ID: `11419757`)

Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
11419757:
Common formulas for the CPRI, eCPRI and OBSAI cases
Denoting by QIQ-in the number of bits in the fractional part for I and Q samples at the input of L1-Hi (CPRI input in the CPRI case, or output of the IQ decompression stage in the eCPRI case), we can have a unique formula for the power unit in the Rx chain, namely (in mW):

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is a fraction. The numerator is enclosed in parentheses and raised to the power of 2. Inside the parentheses, there is a term $2^{Q\_{IQ-in}}$ multiplied by 10 raised to the power of a fraction. The fraction in the exponent has $0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor$ in the numerator and 20 in the denominator. The denominator of the main fraction is $scaler^2$.
The text in the image is:
$$ \left( 2^{Q\_{IQ-in}} \cdot 10^{\frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20}} \right)^2 $$
$$ \frac{}{scaler^2} $$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3127.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.4.4-1)

**with Q**IQ-in **= 14 in the both CPRI case and eCPRI case.**\*\*\*\*

The power unit, expressed in dBm, then is:

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in a light gray font on a white background. The equation is presented in two lines.
The first line reads:
`powerUnit_dBm = 10 * log10( (2^Q_IQ-in * (0.1 * rxScalingFactor / 20))^2 / scaler^2 )`
The second line reads:
`= 0.1 * rxscalingFactor + 20 * log10(2^Q_IQ-in) - 20 * log10(scaler)`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3127.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1](equation 2.5.4.4-2)

*equation 2.5.4.4-1 will be used to derive* equations in section [11419826](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-epfvvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) with slightly different notations (the factor depending on QIQ-in being incorporated in scalerChannelType in *section [11419826](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-epfvvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) rather than being kept separate).*\*\*

---

Denoting by QIQ-in the number of bits in the fractional part for I and Q samples at the input of L1-Hi (CPRI input in the CPRI case, or output of the IQ decompression stage in the eCPRI case), we can have a unique formula for the power unit in the Rx chain, namely (in mW):

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is a fraction. The numerator is enclosed in parentheses and raised to the power of 2. Inside the parentheses, there is a term $2^{Q\_{IQ-in}}$ multiplied by 10 raised to the power of a fraction. The fraction in the exponent has $0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor$ in the numerator and 20 in the denominator. The denominator of the main fraction is $scaler^2$.
The text in the image is:
$$ \left( 2^{Q\_{IQ-in}} \cdot 10^{\frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20}} \right)^2 $$
$$ \frac{}{scaler^2} $$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3130.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.4.4-1)

**with Q**IQ-in **= 14 in the CPRI case and Q**IQ-in **= 15 in both the eCPRI case and** the OBSAI case.***\******\***

The power unit, expressed in dBm, then is:

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in a light gray font on a white background. The equation is presented in two lines.
The first line reads:
`powerUnit_dBm = 10 * log10( (2^Q_IQ-in * (0.1 * rxScalingFactor / 20))^2 / scaler^2 )`
The second line reads:
`= 0.1 * rxscalingFactor + 20 * log10(2^Q_IQ-in) - 20 * log10(scaler)`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3130.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1](equation 2.5.4.4-2)

*equation 2.5.4.4-1 will be used to derive* equations in section [11419826](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-epfvvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) with slightly different notations (the factor depending on QIQ-in being incorporated in scalerChannelType in *section [11419826](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-epfvvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) rather than being kept separate).*\*\*

Above requirement support based on technology and HW board as below table:

|  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Technology** | **ABIO** | **ABIN** | **ASOE** | **ASOF** | **RINLINE1** |
| FR1-FDD-OBSAI | supported | supported | supported | - | - |
| FR1-FDD-CPRI | supported | supported | supported | **[CB009223-C] supported** [End CB009223-C]\*\*\*\* | - |
| FR1-FDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | - | - | supported |
| FR1-TDD-CPRI | supported | - | supported | **[CB009223-D] supported** [End CB009223-D]\*\*\*\* | - |
| FR1-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | supported | supported | supported | supported |
| FR2-TDD-CPRI | - | - | - | - | - |
| FR2-TDD-7-2a-eCPRI | supported | - | - | - | - |

RINLINE 1 support is terminated in 24R1, requirement is not valid for RINLINE 1 starting from 24R2.

Denoting by QIQ-in the number of bits in the fractional part for I and Q samples at the input of L1-Hi (CPRI input in the CPRI case, or output of the IQ decompression stage in the eCPRI case), we can have a unique formula for the power unit in the Rx chain, namely (in mW):

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical expression. The expression is a fraction. The numerator is enclosed in parentheses and raised to the power of 2. Inside the parentheses, there is a term $2^{Q\_{IQ-in}}$ multiplied by 10 raised to the power of a fraction. The fraction in the exponent has $0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor$ in the numerator and 20 in the denominator. The denominator of the main fraction is $scaler^2$.
The text in the image is:
$$ \left( 2^{Q\_{IQ-in}} \cdot 10^{\frac{0.1 \cdot rxScalingFactor}{20}} \right)^2 $$
$$ \frac{}{scaler^2} $$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3132.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.4.4-1)

**with Q**IQ-in **= 14 in CPRI case and Q**IQ-in **= 15 in both eCPRI case and**OBSAI case.***\******\***

The power unit, expressed in dBm, then is:

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in a light gray font on a white background. The equation is presented in two lines.
The first line reads:
`powerUnit_dBm = 10 * log10( (2^Q_IQ-in * (0.1 * rxScalingFactor / 20))^2 / scaler^2 )`
The second line reads:
`= 0.1 * rxscalingFactor + 20 * log10(2^Q_IQ-in) - 20 * log10(scaler)`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3132.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1](equation 2.5.4.4-2)

*equation 2.5.4.4-1 will be used to derive* equations in section [11419826](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-epfvvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) with slightly different notations (the factor depending on QIQ-in being incorporated in scalerChannelType in *section [11419826](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-epfvvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) rather than being kept separate).*\*\*

## 2.5.5 Computations in L1-SW

### 2.5.5.0-1 Computations in L1-SW Power values reported by L1-SW to 5G-L2-PS are usually in dBm, not in mW. Two exceptions are shortTermTaPeakAmp (which, in spite of what “Amp” in its name might suggest, is a power value, not an amplitude) and PeakMetric. shortTermTaPeakAmp and PeakMetric are reported to 5G-L2-PS in arbitrary linear units (not mW). If, for a given ChannelType (ChannelType here is a generic name that stands for either PUSCH, SRS, PUCCH or PRACH), real numbers A, B, …, representing powers in linear scale, need to be converted to dBm by L1-SW before being sent to 5G-L2-PS, the following formulas will be used: (ID: 11419830)

### 2.5.5.1 For Loner only

#### 2.5.5.1.1 Power unit computation

**2.5.5.1.1.0-1**  (ID: `11419873`)

Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:

11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
11419873:
Power unit computation
For traffic channel type:

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray font on a white background. The formula is:
`scalerChannelType = 2^(3-agcShiftChannelType) * alphaAgcChannelType * xScale * 2^-(shift+Q1q-in)`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3137.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.5.1-1)

For PRACH (TDD only):

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula. The formula is:
$scalerPrach = \frac{decimationFactor \cdot 2^{-\frac{max\_shift+mPower\_shift}{2}} \cdot 2^{-(shift+Q\_{IQ-in})}}{postFftScalingFactor \cdot postIfftScalingFactor}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3137.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.5.1-2)

Then

[image-2][image\_desc]scalerChannelType\_dB = 20 \* log₁₀(scalerChannelType)[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3137.003.png[/image\_path][/image-2]    (equation 2.5.5.1-3)

For the CPRI case (Except for PRACH), as stated in section [11418821](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-a_E_vvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ),  unnormalized FFT is performed, the Power conservation rule follows below Parseval’s equation

[image-3][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation states that the sum of the squared magnitudes of a discrete-time signal $x(n)$ from $n=0$ to $N\_{FFT}-1$ is equal to $\frac{1}{N\_{FFT}}$ times the sum of the squared magnitudes of its Discrete Fourier Transform (DFT), $X(k)$, from $k=0$ to $N\_{FFT}-1$. This is a statement of Parseval's theorem for the DFT.
The equation is written as:
$$ \sum\_{n=0}^{N\_{FFT}-1} |x(n)|^2 = \frac{1}{N\_{FFT}} \sum\_{k=0}^{N\_{FFT}-1} |X(k)|^2 $$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3137.004.png[/image\_path][/image-3]    (equation 2.5.5.1-4)

And rxScalingFactor represents average time domain power over the I and Q samples of an OFDM symbol with respect to the system full bandwidth, so taking the FFT processing gain (including fftScalingFactor due to unnormalized FFT) into account to get power unit,

[image-4][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in a light gray font against a white background. The equation is:
`powerUnitChannelType_dBm = 0.1 rxScalingFactor - 20 log10(N_FFT) - scalerChannelType_dB`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3137.005.png[/image\_path][/image-4]    (equation 2.5.5.1-5)

For the eCPRI case, rxScalingFactor represents average frequency domain power over the I and Q samples of an OFDM symbol with respect to the bandwidth of one sub carrier, so the power unit shall be

[image-5][image\_desc]The image contains a single line of text. The text is: `power Unit ChannelType_dBm = 0.1 rxScalingFactor - scalerChannelType_dB`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3137.006.png[/image\_path][/image-5]    (equation 2.5.5.1-6)

**Note: For PRACH, small deviations to the general pattern of calculations presented in this section are introduced, due to the fact that PRACH Rx processing has some differences with the processing of other channels. These deviations will be become apparent in section [11420487](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_e-gepvvvEe-AqvopbP1qhQ).**

For CPRI case and OBSAI case:

For traffic channel type

`scalerChannelType = inputGainChannelType · 2^-(IQ-in)`[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3143.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.5.2-1)
