scalerRIM$*{dB}$ = 20 ⋅ log$*{10}$ (scalerRIM)[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3236.009.png[/image\_path][/image-10]  (equation 2.5.11.1.3-2)

And to convert the final power report to dBm value,

[image-11][image\_desc]powerUnitRIM$*{dB}$ = 0.1 powerScalingFactor - scalerRIM$*{dB}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3236.010.png[/image\_path][/image-11]   (equation 2.5.11.1.3-3)

Calculation of RSSI per symbol and subband, average on all antennas and normalized to 1 PRB, unit dBm:

[image-12][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light blue font against a white background. The formula is:
RSSI (dBm) = 10log10(RSSI(nonScaled)) + powerUnitRIM\_dBm
The formula appears to be related to signal strength measurement, specifically Received Signal Strength Indicator (RSSI) in dBm. It shows how to convert a non-scaled RSSI value to dBm by applying a logarithmic transformation and adding a power unit offset.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3236.011.png[/image\_path][/image-12]    (equation 2.5.11.1.3-4)

Calculation of RIM-RS signal power per symbol, average on all antennas and normalized to 1 PRB, unit dBm:

[image-13][image\_desc]signalPower (dBm) = 10log10 (signalPower (nonScaled)) + powerUnitRIMdBm[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3236.012.png[/image\_path][/image-13]    (equation 2.5.11.1.3-5)

Above formulas shall be performed by L1 ULPHY for RIM RSSI and signalPower **calculation, when only zero-valued samples are got from radio for all the receiving antennas, or in case of noisy measurement (refer [11109713](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_ko7J9_vSEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) and [11109729](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_ko7J_fvSEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)), RSSI and signalPower will be filled with predefined value – 140 dBm.**

• DMRS of all UE are located at the first OFDM symbol, then only the first symbol will be scaled.

• DMRS of all UE are located at the same OFDM symbols, then those symbols having DMRS will be scaled independently.

• DMRS of different UE are located at different OFDM symbols, then those symbols having DMRS will be scaled independently.

Only the nShift calculated from the first DMRS symbol shall be used for the calculation of power measurements since these measurements are based on only the first DMRS symbol.

Calculation of de-boosted RSSI on all Rx “physical” antenna ports, normalized to 1 PRB, unit dBm:

[image-12][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation written in a light gray font against a white background. The equation is:
$RSSI\_{ant (nonScaled,de-boosted)} = \frac{RSSI\_{ant (nonScaled)} - noisePower\_{ant (nonScaled)}}{DMRS\_{BoostPUSCH}} + noisePower\_{ant (nonScaled)}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3229.014.png[/image\_path][/image-12]   (equation 2.5.11.2.1-5)

[image-13][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray color against a white background. The formula is presented on two lines.
The first line reads:
RSSI$*{ant}$ (de-boosted) (dBm)
The second line reads:
= 10log10(RSSI$*{ant}$ (nonScaled.de-boosted)) + powerUnitPusch$\_{dBm}$ + pCorPusch[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3229.015.png[/image\_path][/image-13](equation 2.5.11.2.1-6)

[image-14][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is:
$RSSI\_{(nonScaled.de-boosted)} = \sum\_{ant=0}^{N\_{RX}-1} RSSI\_{ant (nonScaled.de-boosted)}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3229.016.png[/image\_path][/image-14]    (equation 2.5.11.2.1-7)

[image-15][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray font against a white background. The formula is:
RSSI(de-boosted) (dBm) = 10log10(RSSI(nonScaled.de-boosted)) + powerUnit Pusch\_dBm + pCorPusch
The formula appears to be related to signal strength measurements, possibly in a telecommunications context, given the terms "RSSI" (Received Signal Strength Indicator), "dBm" (decibels relative to one milliwatt), and "Pusch" (Physical Uplink Shared Channel). The formula calculates the de-boosted RSSI in dBm by taking the base-10 logarithm of the non-scaled de-boosted RSSI, and then adding two correction terms: "powerUnit Pusch\_dBm" and "pCorPusch".[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3229.017.png[/image\_path][/image-15]    (equation 2.5.11.2.1-8)

Calculation of the received signal power on all Rx “physical” antenna ports, normalized to 1 PRB, unit dBm:

[image-16][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is:
$rxPower\_{ant (nonScaled)} = \frac{RSSI\_{ant (nonScaled)} - noisePower\_{ant (nonScaled)}}{DMRS\_{BoostPUSCH}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3229.018.png[/image\_path][/image-16]    (equation 2.5.11.2.1-9)

[image-17][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray color against a white background. The formula is:
rxPower$*{ant}$ (dBm) = 10log10(rxPower$*{ant}$ (nonscaled)) + powerUnitPusch$\_{dBm}$ + pCorPusch
The formula appears to be related to signal processing or telecommunications, likely calculating the received power at an antenna in dBm.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3229.019.png[/image\_path][/image-17]    (equation 2.5.11.2.1-10)

[image-18][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical equation. The equation is:
$rxPower\_{(nonScaled)} = \frac{RSSI\_{(nonScaled)} - noisePower\_{(nonScaled)}}{DMRS\_{BoostPUSCH}}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3229.020.png[/image\_path][/image-18]    (equation 2.5.11.2.1-11)

[image-19][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light blue color against a white background. The formula is:
rxPower(dBm) = 10log10(rxPower(nonscaled)) + powerUnit Puschasm + pCorPusch
The formula appears to be related to power calculations, possibly in a telecommunications or signal processing context, given the terms "rxPower" (received power), "dBm" (decibels relative to one milliwatt), and "Pusch" (Physical Uplink Shared Channel, a term used in LTE/5G). The term "nonscaled" suggests that the initial received power value is not yet adjusted for certain factors. "powerUnit" and "pCorPusch" likely represent other power components or correction factors.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3229.021.png[/image\_path][/image-19]    (equation 2.5.11.2.1-12)

Where [image-20][image\_desc]The image contains the text "DMRS BoostPUSCH". The text is in a light blue color against a white background. The text is slightly blurry.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3229.022.png[/image\_path][/image-20] = 2 in case of number of DMRS CDM groups without data equal to 2, and [image-21][image\_desc]The image contains the text "DMRS BoostPUSCH". The Rx power scaling formulas for ***\*eCPRI 7-2e RIM are implemented as follows:***\*

Calculation of scalerRIM:

[Before CB012115-SR-HE]

[image-0][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray font against a white background. The formula is:
`scaler RIM = 2^-comExp . 2^nShift . 2^-(qIQ-in)`
The text is slightly blurry, but the characters and symbols are discernible. The formula appears to be a definition or an equation related to scaling or a RIM (Range Image Map) in a technical or scientific context.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3236.001.png[/image\_path][/image-0]    (equation 2.5.11.1.3-1)

[CB012115-SR-HE]

[image-1][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light gray font against a white background. The formula is:
`scaler Rim = 2staticLShift-staticRShift. 2-comExp. 2nShift. 2-(Q1Q-in)`
The text is slightly blurry, but the characters are mostly discernible. The formula appears to be a definition or an equation related to scaling or a similar concept in a technical or scientific context.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3236.002.png[/image\_path][/image-1]    (equation 2.5.11.1.3-1)

[End CB012115-SR-HE]

scalerRIM$*{dB}$ = 20 ⋅ log$*{10}$ (scalerRIM)[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3235.006.png[/image\_path][/image-8]   (equation 2.5.11.2.3-2)

And to convert the final power report to dBm value,

[image-9][image\_desc]powerUnitRIM$*{dB}$ = 0.1 powerScalingFactor - scalerRIM$*{dB}$[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3235.007.png[/image\_path][/image-9]   (equation 2.5.11.2.3-3)

Please refer section [12582454](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_oDsHkDRwEfCKaNlcHOQWmg) for the value of powerScalingFactor.

Calculation of RSSI per symbol and subband,  average on all antennas and normalized to 1 PRB, unit dBm:

[image-10][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in a light blue font on a white background. The formula is:
RSSI (dBm) = 10log10(RSSI (nonScaled)) + powerUnitRIM dBm
The formula appears to be a conversion or calculation related to Received Signal Strength Indicator (RSSI) values, likely in the context of wireless communication. The term "dBm" indicates decibels relative to one milliwatt, a common unit for measuring power levels. "RSSI (nonScaled)" suggests an initial, unadjusted reading, which is then processed using a logarithmic function and an offset ("powerUnitRIM dBm") to arrive at the final RSSI value in dBm.[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3235.008.png[/image\_path][/image-10]    (equation 2.5.11.2.3-4)

Calculation of RIM-RS signal power per symbol,  average on all antennas and normalized to 1 PRB, unit dBm:

[image-11][image\_desc]The image contains a mathematical formula written in light blue text on a white background. The formula is:
signalPower (dBm) = 10log10 (signalPower (nonScaled)) + powerUnitRIMdBm[/image\_desc][image\_path]https://storage.googleapis.com/dng\_files/images/HTML\_pukkola\_5G\_L1\_Entity\_Level\_file\_3235.009.png[/image\_path][/image-11]    (equation 2.5.11.2.3-5)

Above formulas shall be performed by L1 ULPHY for RIM RSSI and signalPower **calculation, when only zero-valued samples are got from radio for all the receiving antennas, or in case of noisy measurement (refer [11109713](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_ko7J9_vSEe-AqvopbP1qhQ) and [11109729](https://dn-prod.ext.net.nokia.com/rm/resources/BI_ko7J_fvSEe-AqvopbP1qhQ)), RSSI and signalPower will be filled with predefined value – 140 dBm.**
